The Obligation of Salawat upon the Prophet
Commentary on the khutbah explaining the obligation of salawat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending salawat upon the Prophet, identify the Quranic and hadith evidence, and explain the basis for the obligation.

Core Idea
The imperative in Quran 33:56 makes salawat upon the Prophet wajib in the Hanafi school.

This passage expands on the opening of the book, focusing on the command to send blessings and peace upon the Prophet (ﷺ). The commentator presents the primary evidence from the Quran and hadith, and clarifies the Hanafi position that this act is a binding obligation, not merely recommended. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct practice and respect for the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the hukm level for sending salawat upon the Prophet: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or mubah? The passage clearly states it is wajib based on the imperative.
Distinguish between fard and wajib: fard is from qat'i dalil, wajib from zanni dalil.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse 33:56 is the main proof. Note the imperative form 'sallu' and 'sallimu'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator. Explain why this verse carries that weight.
The thubut is qati, dalala is zanni, hence wajib not fard.
4
Examine the hadith support
The hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi teaches the specific formula and reinforces the command. Note that the Companions asked 'how' not 'whether'.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and its thamarah
The Shafi'i school holds it as sunnah. Compare the practical consequence: sin vs. no sin for omission.
The Hanafi tarjih is that it is wajib at least once in a lifetime.

Source Text

(4) The Sheikh, the Imam, the Most Glorious, the Ascetic, Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Baghdadi said: Seeking forgiveness. And if it is towards a human being, its meaning is supplication. Peace: every kind of safety. The proof of salawat and salam is in this verse: "Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet. O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace" (Surah al-Ahzab 33:56). Translation: Allah and the angels send salawat upon the Prophet, so O believers, send salawat and salam upon him. This verse commands reciting both salawat and salam. Rather, the distinction is that Allah Himself does this act. Then what can be said of its virtue! The scholars say that the virtue of salawat and salam is greater than when the angels were commanded to prostrate to Adam, because salawat and salam are performed by Allah Himself. After God, you are great, short story. In a hadith: Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi informed me that they said, O Messenger of Allah, how should we send salawat upon you? He said: Say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon his wives and his offspring... (Muslim, Book of Prayer upon the Prophet, p. 175, no. 407; Abu Dawud, Book of Prayer upon the Prophet, p. 147, no. 979). Rasul: A prophet upon whom a new sharia and a book is revealed is called a messenger. A prophet is one upon whom a new sharia is not revealed. Therefore, a messenger is superior to a prophet. For this reason, the author, may Allah have mercy on him, used the phrase 'His Messenger' so that respect and honor would be greater. Muhammad: Derived from 'hamd', praised. That is, one in whom praiseworthy virtues are gathered. The one in whom praiseworthy qualities are gathered. The Prophet has many attributive names, but Muhammad and Ahmad are the most famous names. His grandfather named him that. All good qualities are gathered in him, so he became the very embodiment of his name. Al: Derived from 'ahl'. There is a difference of opinion as to whom it refers. One meaning is his family and dependents and offspring. Another meaning is those individuals of his family for whom accepting charity was forbidden; these individuals are included in his 'al', such as the family of Ali, the family of Ja'far, etc. Ashab: Plural of sahib. His companions, those who saw him with faith and ended their lives in faith, all of them are his companions. May salawat and salam be upon all of them.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the opening of the book (khutbat al-kitab), specifically on the phrases 'salawat' and 'salam' that are part of the author's introduction. The commentator begins by explaining that the word 'istighfar' when directed toward Allah means seeking forgiveness, and when directed toward a human means supplication. Then he discusses 'salam' as comprehensive safety. The main proof for the command to send salawat and salam upon the Prophet (ﷺ) is Quran 33:56, where Allah and the angels perform salawat, and the believers are commanded to do likewise. The commentator emphasizes that this command indicates obligation (hukm). He further supports this with a hadith where the Companions asked how to send salawat, and the Prophet taught them a specific formula. The passage then defines key terms: 'Rasul' (a prophet with a new book and sharia) is superior to 'Nabi' (a prophet without a new sharia). 'Muhammad' means 'the praised one' in whom all praiseworthy qualities are gathered. 'Al' (family) refers to those for whom charity is forbidden, like the family of Ali. 'Ashab' are the Companions who saw the Prophet with faith and died in faith. The entire passage underscores the high status of the Prophet and the obligation of honoring him through salawat and salam.

Key Terms
صلوۃ (salawat): Blessings from Allah (mercy and praise), from angels (supplication), and from believers (prayer for mercy and exaltation).
سلام (salam): Peace and security; the greeting of peace.
رسول (rasul): A prophet to whom a new divine law (sharia) and a book is revealed.
نبی (nabi): A prophet who is not given a new sharia or book, but follows the previous messenger's law.
آل (al): The family of the Prophet, specifically those for whom accepting charity is forbidden (like the families of Ali, Ja'far, etc.).
اصحاب (ashab): The Companions of the Prophet who saw him with faith and died in that state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sending salawat and salam upon the Prophet (ﷺ) when his name is mentioned?
A) Sunnah Mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat upon the Prophet is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, based on the clear command in the Quran and the teachings of the Prophet.

Wiping the Ears in Wudu: Sunnah with the Head
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the ears in wudu, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i position of using separate water.

Core Idea
The ears are part of the head; wiping them with the head's water is sunnah, not a separate act.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: how should the ears be wiped in wudu? The Hanafi school holds that the ears are included in the head wipe, citing the explicit hadith, 'The ears are from the head.' Imam al-Shafi'i, however, regards taking fresh water for the ears as recommended, based on another narration. Understanding this difference requires careful analysis of hadith evidence and principles of legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
The text states that wiping the ears is the sixth sunnah of wudu. Determine the precise hukm level and how the ears are wiped according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah; the method is wiping with the same water used for the head.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Two hadiths are cited: the Prophet wiped his head and ears together, and he said 'the ears are from the head.' Analyze how these prove the Hanafi position.
The phrase 'al-udhunani min al-ra's' is the key textual evidence.
3
Study the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that separate water is masnun (recommended). Identify his evidence from the hadith of Abdullah bin Zaid.
The Shafi'i proof is based on the action of taking new water for the ears.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is implicit: the explicit statement of the Prophet overrides the general action. Understand why Hanafis consider their evidence stronger.
The rebuttal relies on the principle that an explicit statement (nass) takes precedence over a general action.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual practice: Hanafis wipe ears with head water; Shafi'is take fresh water. This difference arises from different interpretations of the same Sunnah.
There is no disagreement on the obligation, only on the sunnah method.

Source Text

(١٠) ومسح الاذنين ( ا ا ) وتخليل اللحية (۱۲) والاصابع (۱۳) وتكرار الغسل الى (۱۰) چھٹی سنت ) دونوں کانوں کا مسح کرنا ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه و سلم مسح برأسه واذنيه ظاهرهما و باطنهما (ترمذی شریف، باب مسح الاذنین ظاهرها بالمنهما ص ۱۶ نمبر ۳۶ / ابوداؤد، باب صفة وضوء النبی ص ۶ نمبر (۱۲) انه مسح براسه وقال الاذنان من الرأس (الف) (ترمذی، باب ما جاء ان الاذنین من الراس نمبر ۳۷) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ کان کے اوپر اور نیچے کا حصہ سر کے ساتھ مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔ فائده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کان کے لئے الگ پانی لینا مسنون ہے۔ اور شعمی [؟] فرماتے ہیں کہ آگے کا حصہ چہرے کے ساتھ دھویا جائے اور کان کے پیچھے کا حصہ سر کے ساتھ دھویا جائے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سمع عبد الله بن زيد يذكر انه راى رسول الله يتوضأ فاخذ لاذنيه ماء خلاف الماء الذي اخذ لرأسه (سنن بیھقی ، باب مسح الاذنین بماء جدید ج اول ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۳۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کان کے لئے الگ پانی لیا۔
The sixth sunnah) is wiping both ears. In hadith: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped his head and his ears, their outer and inner parts' (Tirmidhi..., Abu Dawud...). And he wiped his head and said: 'The two ears are from the head' (Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is proven that wiping the upper and lower part of the ear with the head is sunnah. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i says that taking separate water for the ears is recommended (masnun). And Shami [؟] says: the front part is washed with the face, and the back part of the ear is wiped with the head. Imam Shafi'i's evidence is this hadith: 'I heard Abdullah bin Zaid mention that he saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu, so he took for his ears water different from the water he took for his head' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This hadith states that separate water was taken for the ears.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling of wiping the ears in wudu. The author begins by stating that wiping the ears is the sixth sunnah of wudu. He then provides proof from two hadiths: the Prophet wiped his ears together with his head and explicitly stated that the ears are part of the head. Therefore, in the Hanafi school, the ears are wiped with the same water used for the head, not with fresh water. The passage then reports a difference of opinion: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is recommended (masnun) to take fresh water for the ears, citing the hadith of Abdullah bin Zaid. The author also mentions a third opinion attributed to 'Shami' (possibly a misprint for al-Shafi'i or another scholar) that the front part of the ear is washed with the face and the back part with the head. The Hanafi response is implicit: the stronger evidence is the explicit hadith that the ears are part of the head, so separate water is not needed. The ruling in the Hanafi school is that wiping the ears with the water of the head is sunnah; taking fresh water is not required and is not considered sunnah.

Key Terms
مسح (mas-h): Wiping with wet hands over a body part without running water.
الاذنان من الرأس (al-udhunani min al-ra's): The ears are considered part of the head in the context of wudu.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed; omission does not invalidate wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping the ears in wudu?
A) It is fard (obligatory) to wipe the ears with fresh water.
B) It is sunnah to wipe the ears with the same water used for the head.
C) It is wajib to wipe the ears separately.
D) Wiping the ears is not part of wudu.

Key Takeaway
The ears are part of the head in wudu; Hanafis wipe them with the head's water, and this is a confirmed sunnah.

Khilal of the Beard in Wudu
States khilal of beard is sunnah and provides proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when khilal of the beard is sunnah vs. necessary in Hanafi wudu, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Khilal of a thick beard is sunnah; for a thin beard, water must reach the skin.

This lesson examines the seventh sunnah of wudu: khilal of the beard. The Hanafi school distinguishes between thick and thin beards, affecting whether khilal is merely recommended or required. We will explore the hadith evidence and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that khilal of the beard is a sunnah act of wudu. Determine the specific hukm level.
The act is khilal, and the initial ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: from Uthman that the Prophet used to do khilal, and from Anas with the statement 'Thus my Lord commanded me.'
Both are from reliable sources (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice and his statement indicate a recommended act. The command is not understood as obligating the umma because it is a personal practice or a sunnah.
Hanafis distinguish between commands that establish obligation vs. recommendation.
4
Apply the distinction between thick and thin beard
The note clarifies: for a thin beard, water must reach the skin (wajib as part of face washing); for a thick beard, washing the outer part suffices and khilal is sunnah.
Thin beard = skin visible; thick beard = skin not visible.
5
Note the practical consequence
A worshipper must assess beard thickness. If thin, ensure water reaches skin; if thick, perform khilal as sunnah but it is not obligatory.
Omission of khilal for thick beard does not invalidate wudu; omission of water under thin beard does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١) [ ساتویں سنت ] ڈاڑھی کو خلال کرنا ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن عثمان بن عفان ان النبي صلى الله عليه و سلم كان يخلل لحيته ( ترمذی شریف ، باب تخلیل اللحیۃ ص ۱۴ نمبر (۳) عن
انس بن مالک ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه و سلم كان اذا توضأ اخذ كفا من ماء فادخله تحت حنكه خلل به لحيته وقال هكذا
امرنی ربی (ب) (ابوداؤد، باب تخلیل اللحیۃ ص ۲۱ نمبر ۱۴۵) نوٹ ہلکی ڈاڑھی ہو تو پانی خال تک پہنچانا ضروری ہے۔ اور گھنی ڈاڑھی ہو تو ڈاڑھی کے اوپر دھولے اور ڈاڑھی کے اندر خلال کرنا اس وقت سنت ہے۔
The seventh sunnah) is to perform khilal of the beard. In hadith: 'From Uthman ibn Affan that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform khilal of his beard' (Tirmidhi). And from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he performed wudu, he took a handful of water and put it under his chin, then he performed khilal of his beard with it, and said: 'Thus my Lord commanded me' (Abu Dawud). Note: If the beard is thin, it is necessary to make water reach the skin. And if the beard is thick, then washing the top of the beard and performing khilal inside the beard at that time is sunnah.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the seventh sunnah of wudu: khilal of the beard. The author presents two hadiths: one from Uthman that the Prophet regularly did khilal of his beard, and another from Anas that the Prophet took water under his chin and combed his beard with it, saying 'Thus my Lord commanded me.' The note clarifies the application: if the beard is thin, water must reach the skin (this is wajib to ensure complete washing of the face area). If the beard is thick, it is sufficient to wash the outer part; the inner khilal is then sunnah, not obligatory. This is a Hanafi precision: the obligation is only to wash the apparent part of the beard; khilal of a thick beard is a sunnah act for completeness.

Key Terms
خلال (khilal): Passing wet fingers through the beard to ensure water reaches between hairs.
ہلکی ڈاڑھی (halki dadhi): A thin beard where the skin is visible underneath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for khilal of the beard for a person with a thick beard?
A) It is wajib (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah
C) It is haram
D) It is not part of wudu

Key Takeaway
Khilal of the beard is sunnah for thick beards, but for thin beards water must reach the skin as part of washing the face.

The Eighth Sunnah of Wudu: Khilal of the Fingers
States the ruling of khilal as sunnah with proof and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khilal of the fingers in wudu according to the Hanafi school, identify its proof from hadith, and explain the wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
Khilal of the fingers is a sunnah that ensures water reaches every part, as even a hair's breadth of dryness invalidates wudu.

In this lesson, we examine the eighth sunnah of wudu: khilal (passing water between) the fingers and toes. The text provides a clear hadith command and explains why this practice is important for the validity of wudu. Understanding this ruling helps you perfect your wudu according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing khilal of the fingers and toes during wudu. The ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib.
Sunnah muakkadah means it is a confirmed practice of the Prophet; omission is not sinful but disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'When you perform wudu, perform khilal of the fingers of your hands and your feet.' This is recorded in Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
This is a hadith ahad (single-narrator chain), giving it zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'fakhalil' is an imperative. In Hanafi usul, commands in wudu are interpreted as sunnah unless there is evidence for obligation. There is no such evidence here, so khilal is sunnah.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which often interprets such commands as wajib.
4
Explore the wisdom
The wisdom is that khilal ensures water reaches between the fingers and toes, preventing any dry spot. The text states that if even a hair's breadth remains dry, wudu is invalid.
Thus, khilal helps fulfill the condition of complete coverage of the wudu limbs.
5
Compare cross-madhhab perspectives
While the Hanafi school holds khilal as sunnah, some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it wajib. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on how the command is interpreted.
The practical difference is that if omitted, wudu is valid according to Hanafis but invalid according to those who deem it wajib.

Source Text

(۱۲) آٹھویں سنت ) انگلیوں کا خلال کرنا ہے۔

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof for the eighth sunnah: khilal of the fingers of both hands and feet. The hadith from Ibn Abbas is a direct command from the Prophet. The author explains the rationale: khilal ensures that no part of the fingers remains dry, as even a hair's breadth of dryness invalidates wudu. This underscores the importance of thoroughness in wudu. In the Hanafi school, khilal of the fingers is considered sunnah, not wajib, but it is strongly recommended because it assures full coverage of the limbs.

Three Repetitions in Wudu
States three repetitions is sunnah with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating wudu limb washing (sunnah muakkadah) and identify the hadith proof and its legal implication.

Core Idea
Washing each limb three times in wudu is a confirmed sunnah; once fulfills the obligation.

In this passage, the author explains the ninth sunnah of wudu—repeating each wash three times. He clarifies the crucial distinction between fard (once) and sunnah (three times) and supports it with the famous hadith of Uthman ibn Affan, which describes the Prophet's wudu. This lesson will help you understand the legal weight of three repetitions and how to apply the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the hukm (legal ruling) of washing each limb three times in wudu according to this passage? The author states it is sunnah.
Sunnah muakkadah is the level.
2
Distinguish levels of obligation
The passage distinguishes between washing once (fard) and three times (sunnah). Understand that the fard is the minimum requirement; the sunnah is recommended for completeness.
This distinction prevents confusion about validity.
3
Locate the dalil
Which evidence is cited? The hadith of Uthman ibn Affan, which the author quotes partially. Identify the source (Bukhari, Abu Dawud).
The hadith is a key proof text in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the sunnah status? The Prophet explicitly demonstrated three repetitions, so his action is a proof (fi‘l) indicating recommendation, not obligation.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action shows sunnah unless it is clarified as wajib.
5
Note the mufta bihi
What is the relied-upon position for fatwa? Three times is sunnah; washing more than three is makruh tanzihi.
This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

The ninth sunnah) is to repeat washing three times. (1) Washing the limbs once is fard, and washing three times is sunnah. Washing three times gives certainty that no place the width of a hair remains dry. (2) In hadith: 'I saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, then he poured water on his palms three times and washed them, then he put his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times, and his arms to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times to the ankles. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the ninth sunnah: repeating the washing of each limb three times. The author clarifies that washing once is fard (obligatory); three times is sunnah. The rationale is to ensure complete coverage. The proof is the famous hadith of Uthman, which describes the Prophet's wudu in detail with three repetitions. In the Hanafi school, the three repetitions are considered a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah). If one washes only once, wudu is valid but the sunnah is missed. Washing more than three times is discouraged (makruh) as it exceeds the Prophet's practice.

In the Hanafi school, washing each limb three times in wudu is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), while washing once fulfills the obligatory (fard) component.

Intention in Wudu: Sunnah or Fard?
States intention in wudu as mustahab with proofs and rebuttal of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in wudu, identify the three proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Water purifies by itself; intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard.

This lesson examines the status of intention (niyyah) in wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author classifies it as mustahab (or sunnah), presenting three dalils that water is inherently purifying, and then addresses the Shafi'i position that intention is fard based on the hadith of intentions. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the difference between validity and reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi classification
Note that intention in wudu is sunnah (mustahab), not fard. Reward is gained but omission does not invalidate.
Early Hanafis used mustahab interchangeably with sunnah.
2
Examine the first proof: Quranic verse
Allah says: 'We sent down from the sky pure water' (25:48). The word 'tahuran' indicates a purifying quality inherent in water, independent of intention.
The verse's literal meaning is the basis.
3
Examine the second proof: Hadith of seawater
The Prophet said: 'It (seawater) is purifying, its dead is halal.' This shows water purifies by itself, without the need for intention.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi.
4
Examine the third proof: Incident of Umar
Umar performed wudu while in a state of disbelief to touch the Quran. Since disbelievers do not have valid intention, this wudu was valid, proving intention is not a condition.
This incident is cited in Hanafi works.
5
Address the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'Actions are by intentions,' interpreting it as requiring intention for validity. Hanafis respond that the hadith concerns reward, not validity; water's purifying power is unaffected by intention.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi wudu is valid without intention; Shafi'i wudu is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستحبات وضو کا بیان
ضروری نوٹ : مستحب اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ کرنے پر ثواب دیا جائے اور نہ کرنے پر کوئی عتاب نہ ہو۔ مصنف نے نیت کرنا، پورے سر کا مسح کرنا، ترتیب سے وضوء کرنا اور پے در پے وضو کرنا مستحب لکھا ہے۔ حالانکہ دوسری کتابوں میں ان کو سنت کہا ہے ( کمانی الہدایہ ) اور احادیث سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ یہ چار باتیں سنت ہیں۔ متقدمین کے یہاں سنت کو بھی مستحب کہہ دیا کرتے تھے اس اعتبار سے مصنف نے ان چاروں کو مستحب کہا ہے۔ البتہ دائیں جانب سے شروع کرنا اور گردن کا مسح کرنا مستحب ہے۔
(۱۴) وضو کرنے والے کے لئے سنت ہے کہ پاکی کی نیت کرے۔ سنت ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے۔ عمر بن خطاب رضي الله عنه على المنبر يقول سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه و سلم يقول انما الاعمال بالنيات وانمالکل امرء ما نوی (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی الی رسول اللہ اللہ ص ۲ نمبر ۱ ) اعمال کے ثواب کا دارو مدار یا اعمال کے صحیح ہونے کا دارومدار نیت پر ہے۔ بغیر نیت کے وضو کا ثواب نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے وضو میں وضو کی نیت کرنا سنت ہے۔ وضو میں نیت کرنا فرض اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ پانی کو خود بخود پاک کرنے والا قرار دیا ہے چاہے نیت کرے یا نہ کرے۔ وی (۱) آیت ہے انزلنا من السماء ماء طهورا ( آیت ۴۸ سورۃ الفرقان (۲۵) (۲) حدیث میں ہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه و سلم هو الطهور ماءه الحل ميتته (ج ) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ماء البحرانه طلبو ص ۲۱ نمبر ۶۹ ) جب پانی بغیر نیت کی قید کے خود بخود پاک کرنے والا ہے تو نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں رہا۔ البتہ حدیث بالا کی وجہ سے سنت رہے گا (۳) حضرت عمر نے قرآن کریم چھونے کے لئے کفر کی حالت میں وضو کیا ہے۔ اور کفر کی حالت میں نیت کا اعتبار نہیں اس لئے ان کا وضو کرنا بغیر نیت کے درست رہا۔ معلوم ہوا کہ وضو کے لئے نیت کی شرط نہیں ہے۔
نماز ، روزہ ، زکوۃ اور حج وغیرہ عبادت مقصودہ میں اصل مقصد ثواب ہے اس لئے بغیر نیت کے یہ عبادات ادا نہ ہوں گی۔ وہاں نیت کرنا فرض ہے۔ ن امام شافعی کے نزدیک حدیث انما الاعمال بالنیات کی وجہ سے وضو میں بھی نیت کرنا فرض ہے (موسوعہ امام شافعی ج اول ، باب النبیہ فی الوضوء)
Statement of the mustahabbat (recommended acts) of wudu. Essential note: Mustahab is something for doing which reward is given and for not doing which there is no punishment. The author has written intention, wiping the entire head, performing wudu in order, and performing wudu consecutively as mustahab. However, in other books they are called sunnah (as in al-Hidayah) and hadiths also indicate that these four are sunnah. The early scholars (mutaqaddimin) used to call sunnah also mustahab; based on that, the author called these four mustahab. However, starting from the right side and wiping the neck are mustahab. (14) It is sunnah for the one performing wudu to intend purification. The reason it is sunnah is this hadith: Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Actions are by intentions, and every man has that which he intended' (Bukhari). The reward or correctness of actions depends on intention. Without intention, there is no reward for wudu. Therefore, intending wudu in wudu is sunnah. Intention in wudu is not fard because water has been declared automatically purifying, whether one intends or not. (1) The verse: 'We sent down from the sky pure water' (Quran 25:48). (2) Hadith: The Prophet said: 'It (seawater) is purifying, its dead (fish) is halal' (Tirmidhi). Since water is automatically purifying without the condition of intention, intention is not necessary. However, due to the aforementioned hadith, it remains sunnah. (3) Umar performed wudu in a state of disbelief for touching the Quran, and in disbelief intention is not considered, so his wudu without intention was valid. Thus it is known that intention is not a condition for wudu. As for prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj and other intended acts of worship, the main objective is reward, so without intention these acts are not performed validly. There, intention is fard. Imam Shafi'i holds that due to the hadith 'actions are by intentions', intention in wudu is also fard.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a definition ruling (defining mustahab) and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding intention in wudu. The author first explains that the term 'mustahab' is used by early Hanafi scholars broadly to include what later scholars call sunnah. The four acts listed (intention, wiping whole head, sequence, and continuity) are considered sunnah in later Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah, but the author of this commentary calls them mustahab due to early usage. Then the main issue: intention in wudu. The Hanafi position is that intention is sunnah (or mustahab), not fard. The author provides three proofs: (1) Quranic verse declaring water purifying (2:48) without conditioning intention; (2) hadith that seawater is purifying without intention; (3) the incident of Umar performing wudu while in a state of disbelief (since he was not a Muslim at that time, his intention would not be valid, yet his wudu was considered good for Quran touching later). These indicate that wudu is valid without intention. However, the hadith of 'actions by intentions' makes intention rewarding, so it is sunnah. The passage contrasts with Imam Shafi'i, who considers intention fard in wudu based on the same hadith. The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, wudu without intention is valid but reward is lacking; in the Shafi'i school, wudu without intention is invalid.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): An act for which there is reward, but no punishment for omission.
نية (niyyah): The intention of the heart to perform an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a proof used by Hanafis to show wudu does not require intention?
A) Quran 25:48
B) Hadith of seawater
C) Hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat'
D) The incident of Umar's wudu in disbelief

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention (niyyah) in wudu is sunnah, not fard; water purifies by itself, but intention brings reward.

Wiping the Neck: A Recommended Act in Wudu
States the ruling of wiping the neck as mustahabb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck during wudu (mustahabb) and identify the evidence supporting its recommendation.

Core Idea
Wiping the neck is mustahabb—not a sunnah—but recommended based on prophetic promise and practice.

In this lesson, you will learn about the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck during wudu. While many acts of wudu are sunnan (recommended practices), wiping the neck holds a slightly lower status: mustahabb. The source passage provides two hadith that encourage this act. We will examine the evidence and understand why the Hanafi school classifies it as mustahabb rather than sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states 'And wiping the neck' as the act. The Hanafi ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
Mustahabb is synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Ibn Umar with a promise of reward, and one from Talha's grandfather showing the Prophet's practice.
Both are ahad hadith, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith explicitly mentions wiping the neck and attaches a reward, indicating desirability. The second shows prophetic action, confirming recommendation.
The promise of reward is a strong indicator of istihbab (recommendation).
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
The Shafi'i school does not consider wiping the neck as part of wudu, making this a matter of ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is mustahabb, not wajib or sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage presents the ruling on wiping the neck during wudu. The text is a ruling statement that it is a recommended act (mustahabb). This is supported by two hadith: the first explicitly states the reward of protection on the Day of Judgment, and the second shows the Prophet's practice of wiping the nape and upper neck. In the Hanafi school, wiping the neck is not a sunnah but a mustahabb, as it is not from the established sunnah practices (sunan) of wudu. The commentator notes that the author enumerated fourteen sunnan; wiping the neck is additional and considered mustahabb.

Nullifiers of Wudu: Two Passages and Bleeding
Defines nullifiers of wudu with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nullifiers of wudu according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between blood that nullifies wudu and blood that does not.

Core Idea
Everything exiting the two passages nullifies wudu; blood, pus, and matter do so only if they flow to a washable area.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi ruling on what breaks wudu. The source passage lists general nullifiers and adds specific impure substances like blood. We will unpack the evidence and clarify the conditions for nullification, especially the Hanafi nuance on bleeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general nullifier
Read the first sentence: 'كل ما خرج من السبيلين' — everything exiting the two passages. This includes urine, feces, wind, etc. Understand that this is the broad category.
The two passages are the front (urinary tract) and the back (anus) for both genders.
2
Note the added nullifiers
The passage adds blood, pus, and matter (دم, قيح, صديد). These are specific impure substances that also nullify wudu, but with conditions.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Verse 5:6 'أو جاء أحد منكم من الغائط' — coming from the toilet implies the need for wudu. This supports the ruling for the two passages.
The Quranic dalil is qat'i in transmission (thubut) but zanni in meaning (dalala) as it only implies the ruling.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The hadith from Safwan mentions that feces, urine, and sleep necessitate wudu. The hadith from Aisha explicitly commands wudu for vomiting, nosebleed, regurgitation, and madhy. The hadith of Fatimah on istihadah shows that continuous bleeding does not nullify wudu if the person is ma'dhur.
5
Understand the Hanafi condition for bleeding
Blood, pus, and matter nullify wudu only if they flow from the wound to a place that requires washing in wudu (موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير). If the blood just appears but does not flow to the exterior, wudu remains valid.
This condition distinguishes the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i, who hold that bleeding never nullifies wudu.

Source Text

(۲۰) والمعانى الناقضة للوضوء كل ما خرج من السبيلين. (۲۱) والدم والقيح والصديد. آية: أو جاء أحد منكم من الغائط أو لمستم النساء. حديث: عن صفوان بن عسال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يأمرنا إذا كنا سفرا أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن إلا من جنابة ولكن من غائط وبول ونوم. حديث: عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من أصابه قيء أو رعاف أو قلس أو مذى فليَنصرف فليتوضأ ثم ليبن على صلاته وهو في ذلك لا يتكلم. حديث: جاءت فاطمة بنت أبي حبيش إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت يا رسول الله إني امرأة أستحاض فلا أطهر أفأدع الصلاة؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا إنما ذلك عرق وليس بحيض فإذا أقبلت حيضتك فدعي الصلاة وإذا أدبرت فاغسلي عنك الدم ثم صلي وقال أبي ثم توضأي لكل صلاة.
(20) And the meanings that nullify wudu: everything that exits from the two passages. (21) And blood, pus, and matter. Verse: 'or if you have come from the place of relieving yourselves or have touched women.' Hadith: From Safwan ibn Assal: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded us when we were traveling not to remove our leather socks for three days and nights except from janabah, but from feces, urine, and sleep. Hadith: From Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever is afflicted with vomiting, nosebleed, regurgitation, or madhy should leave, perform wudu, and then continue his prayer, and he does not speak during that.' Hadith: Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman with istihadah and I do not become pure; should I abandon prayer?' The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'No, that is but a vein and not menstruation. So when your menstruation comes, leave the prayer; and when it passes, wash the blood from yourself and pray.' And he [Abu Bakr?] said: 'Then perform wudu for every prayer.'
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the nullifiers of wudu. It begins with a general statement: everything that exits from the two passages (front and back) nullifies wudu. This includes urine, feces, wind, etc. Then it adds blood, pus, and matter as additional nullifiers when they exit the body and reach a place where purification is required (موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير). The commentary explains that these substances are impure (najis) and their exit breaks wudu unless the person is excused (ma'dhur) due to continuous flow. The proofs include the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) about coming from the toilet, and hadith from Safwan about wiping over socks, indicating that feces and urine necessitate wudu. The hadith from Aisha about vomiting and nosebleed shows that these also nullify wudu. The hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh clarifies that istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) does not nullify wudu for each prayer if the person is ma'dhur (mustahadah) — instead, wudu is required for each prayer time. The Hanafi ruling: bleeding, pus, etc. nullify wudu if they flow from the wound to a place that can be washed in wudu (i.e., the exterior of the body). If the blood merely appears but does not flow, wudu is not nullified.

Key Terms
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (urinary tract) and the back (anus)
موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير (mawḍiʿ yalḥaquhu ḥukm al-taṭhīr): A place on the body where the ruling of purification applies, i.e., an area that is washed during wudu or ghusl
معذور (maʿdhūr): A person excused due to continuous exit of impurities (e.g., constantly bleeding wound), whose wudu is not nullified by that impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does blood from a wound nullify wudu?
A) Whenever it appears on the skin
B) Only if it flows to a place that is washed in wudu (exterior)
C) Never, because blood is not from the two passages
D) Only if it is flowing continuously

Key Takeaway
Blood, pus, and matter nullify wudu in the Hanafi school only when they flow to an area that must be washed during wudu.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Loud Laughter (Qahqaha) in Prayer as a Nullifier of Wudu
Ruling and dispute over loud laughter nullifying wudu and prayer in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qahqaha in prayer, explain the madhhab dispute, and evaluate the Hanafi use of a weak hadith against qiyas.

Core Idea
Loud laughter in prayer breaks both prayer and wudu in the Hanafi school — contrary to analogy, based on a weak hadith.

This passage addresses a unique Hanafi ruling: that loud laughter (qahqaha) during a prayer with ruku and sujud nullifies not only the prayer but also the wudu. This contradicts the general principle that wudu is only broken by physical impurities or loss of intellect. The author presents the evidence from a weak hadith and the opposing view of most other imams who rely on qiyas. The passage also defines three levels of laughter and their effects, and lists the five nullifiers of wudu.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its condition
The Hanafi school holds that loud laughter (qahqaha) in any prayer that includes bowing and prostration (ruku and sujud) nullifies both the prayer and wudu. This does not apply to funeral prayer (janazah), which has no ruku or sujud.
The condition of 'prayers with ruku and sujud' is a key limitation.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Most other imams (including al-Shafi'i) hold that wudu does not break from laughter. Their proof is qiyas: wudu is only broken by exit of impurities or loss of intellect, and laughter does not involve either. They also cite a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet ordered repeating prayer but not wudu.
The opposing school relies on a stronger analogy and a hadith that directly states wudu is not repeated.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa relies on a weak hadith (da'if) from al-Bayhaqi and al-Dar Qutni: when a blind man fell into a well during prayer, some companions laughed, and the Prophet ordered them to repeat both wudu and prayer. Despite its weakness, this hadith is acted upon.
The hadith is not in the Six Books but is accepted by the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Hanafi justification for preferring the weak hadith
The Hanafi school prioritizes ihtiyat (caution) and the principle that a weak hadith may be acted upon if it does not contradict a stronger source. Since no definitive text forbids breaking wudu due to laughter, the weak hadith is taken as binding.
This is a distinctive methodological choice in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In Hanafi practice, one must renew both wudu and prayer after qahqaha in a prayer with ruku/sujud. In other schools, only the prayer is repeated; wudu remains valid.
This difference affects daily worship, especially for Hanafis in mixed-madhhab settings.

Source Text

بالاغماء والجنون (۲۴) والقهقهة فى كل صلوة ذات ركوع و سجود
نوٹ بے ہوشی اور جنون میں بھی عقل زائل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا
اصول زیلان عقل سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے۔ الحج : پہلو کے بل سونا، کروٹ کے بل سونا ۔ الاغماء : بی ہوتی ہونا۔ الجھون : پاگل پن ہونا
(۲۴) قہقہہ مار کر ہنسنار کوع سجدے والی نماز میں ( تو اس سے بھی وضوٹوٹ جائے گا ) تشریح رکوع سجدے والی نماز کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ اگر نماز جنازہ میں قہقہہ مار کر ہنسا تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ صرف نماز ٹوٹے گی قہقہہ مار کر بننے سے بدن سے کوئی نجاست نہیں نکلتی ہے اس لئے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ وضو نہ ٹوٹے۔ چنانچہ اکثر ائمہ کے نزدیک قہقہہ سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹتا ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ ضعیف حدیث سے وضو ٹونا ثابت ہے اس لئے امام ابو حنیفہ تضعیف حدیث پر بھی عمل کر کے وضو ٹوٹنے کے
قائل ہیں۔
حدیث میں ہے ان النبي عل كان يصلي بالناس فدخل اعمى فتردى في بئر كانت في المسجد فضحك طوائف من كان خلف النبي الله في صلواتهم فلما سلم النبى الله الله امر من كان ضحك ان يعيد وضوئه ويعيد صلواته (الف) (سنن البیھقی، باب ترک دالوضوء من القبقبة في الصلوة ، ج اول ص ۲۲۷، نمبر ۶۸۰ ردار قطنی ، باب احادیث القبقبه ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۶۱۴ ) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ زور سے بننے سے نماز تو ٹوٹے گی ہی لیکن وضو بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
ت آہستہ بننے سے صرف نماز ٹوٹے گی اور تبسم سے کچھ نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
نا کہ چونکہ قہقہہ سے وضو ٹا نا خلاف قیاس ہے اس لئے دوسرے ائمہ کے نزدیک اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹتا ہے۔ عن جابر قال يعيد الصلوة ولا يعيد الوضوء (سنن بیہقی ، باب ترك الوضوء من القبقبة فی الصلوۃ ، ج اول ص ۲۵، نمبر۶۷۴) صحاح ستہ میں قہقہہ والی حدیث نہیں ہے۔

With fainting and insanity (24) and loud laughter in every prayer that has bowing and prostration. Note: In unconsciousness and insanity, the intellect is also lost, so wudu will break. Principle: Wudu breaks due to loss of intellect. Al-Hajj: sleeping on the side, sleeping on the back. Al-Ighma': fainting. Al-Junun: madness. (24) Laughing aloud in a prayer with bowing and prostration (then wudu will also break). Explanation: The condition of prayer with bowing and prostration is imposed because if one laughs aloud in funeral prayer, wudu will not break; only the prayer will break. Since laughing aloud does not cause any impurity to exit the body, analogy requires that wudu does not break. Thus, according to most imams, wudu does not break due to laughter. However, since a weak hadith proves that wudu breaks, Imam Abu Hanifa, acting upon the weak hadith, holds that wudu breaks. The hadith states: 'The Prophet ﷺ was leading people in prayer when a blind man entered and fell into a well that was in the mosque. Some of those behind the Prophet ﷺ in prayer laughed. When the Prophet ﷺ said the salam, he ordered those who laughed to repeat their wudu and repeat their prayer.' (Al-Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Tark al-Wudu min al-Qahqaha fi al-Salah, vol. 1, p. 227, no. 680; Dar Qutni, Bab Ahadith al-Qahqaha, p. 175, no. 614). This hadith proves that laughing loudly breaks the prayer and also breaks wudu. Soft laughter only breaks the prayer, and smiling breaks nothing. And because breaking wudu due to laughter is contrary to analogy, other imams hold that wudu does not break from it. From Jabir: 'He repeats the prayer and does not repeat wudu.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Tark al-Wudu min al-Qahqaba fi al-Salah, vol. 1, p. 25, no. 674). The hadith about qahqaha is not in the Six Books. Al-Qahqaha: such laughter that neighbors hear. Al-Hamk: such laughter that one hears oneself. Al-Tabassum: such a smile that neither neighbors nor the person himself hears. Summary: Things that break wudu are of five types: (1) something exits from the two passages, (2) impurity exits from any part of the body, (3) vomit from the mouth, (4) loss of intellect, (5) laughing aloud. Footnote: (b) The Prophet was leading the Companions in prayer when a blind man entered and fell into a well in the mosque. Some of the Companions who were behind the Prophet in prayer laughed. When he said the salam, he ordered those who laughed to renew their wudu and repeat their prayer. Note: Regarding the breaking of prayer due to laughter, Imam Abu Hanifa abandoned analogy and acted upon a weak hadith, acting with caution. This is his perfection of piety. May God have mercy on these pure-hearted lovers.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of loud laughter (qahqaha) during prayer as a nullifier of both prayer and wudu, which is a distinctive Hanafi position. The passage type is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by listing qahqaha among the nullifiers of wudu, specifically in prayers that involve bowing and prostration (i.e., any prayer except funeral prayer). The condition is explained: if one laughs loudly in a funeral prayer, only the prayer breaks, not wudu. Then the author addresses the underlying legal reasoning: laughter does not involve the exit of any impurity, so by analogy (qiyas), wudu should not break. Indeed, most imams (including al-Shafi'i and Malik according to one view) hold that wudu remains intact. However, Imam Abu Hanifa relies on a weak hadith (da'if) in which the Prophet ordered those who laughed during prayer due to a blind man falling into a well to repeat both wudu and prayer. Despite the hadith's weakness, Abu Hanifa acts upon it out of caution (ihtiyat) and because it is not contradicted by a stronger text. The author then defines three levels of laughter: qahqaha (loud enough for neighbors to hear) breaks both prayer and wudu; hamk (moderate laughter heard by oneself) breaks only prayer; tabassum (silent smile) breaks nothing. A summary lists five nullifiers of wudu, including laughter. The footnote reiterates the story and notes Abu Hanifa's piety in preferring a weak hadith over analogy.

Key Terms
قہقہہ (qahqaha): Loud laughter that can be heard by neighbors; specifically in the context of prayer, it nullifies both prayer and wudu.
ھمک (hamk): Moderate laughter that one hears oneself but not neighbors; it nullifies prayer but not wudu.
تبسم (tabassum): Silent smile that produces no sound; does not nullify prayer or wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling on loud laughter (qahqaha) during a funeral prayer (salat al-janazah)?
A) It nullifies both prayer and wudu.
B) It nullifies the prayer but not wudu.
C) It nullifies wudu but not prayer.
D) It does not nullify anything.

Key Takeaway
Loud laughter (qahqaha) in a prayer with ruku and sujud nullifies both the prayer and wudu in the Hanafi school, based on a weak hadith preferred over qiyas.

The True Dawn: Subh Sadiq and Fajr Time
Defines the beginning and end of Fajr time with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define subh sadiq and subh kazib, and state the Hanafi ruling on the beginning of Fajr time with its proof from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins with the true dawn – a horizontal spreading light, not the vertical false dawn.

This lesson marks the start of the Book of Prayer. The author first establishes that time is a condition for prayer, citing Quranic proof. Then he defines the exact moment of Fajr: the appearance of subh sadiq. We will examine the textual evidence distinguishing true dawn from false dawn and understand the Hanafi position on when Fajr prayer becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Fajr prayer is fard 'ayn. The time of Fajr is a condition (shart) for its validity. Without the proper time, the prayer is not valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 4:103 ('prayer has been decreed at specific times') and Quran 20:130 ('exalt before sunrise'). He also cites the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub from Sahih Muslim: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal nor this vertical whiteness fool you until it spreads out.'
The hadith is ahad but accepted in the school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse commands praise before sunrise – understood by the Hanafis to refer to Fajr prayer. The hadith explicitly distinguishes the spreading light (subh sadiq) from the vertical light (subh kazib). The key Arabic term is 'yastatir' (spreads), which indicates the true dawn.
The Hanafi school uses this hadith as the primary textual evidence for the definition of Fajr time.
4
Note the practical application
Subh sadiq marks the beginning of Fajr prayer and the start of fasting. Subh kazib is disregarded. There is minor difference among astronomers on the exact angle (15 vs 18 degrees), but both are based on the same phenomenon.
The mufta bihi position is that Fajr time begins when the spreading light is visible.

كتاب الصلوة
ضروری نوٹ صلوۃ کے لغوی معنی دعا ہے۔ شریعت میں ارکان معہودہ کو صلوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ صلوۃ کے فرض ہونی کی دلیل قرآن کی بہت سی آمیتیں ہیں ۔ مثلا ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا (الف) ( آیت ۳۰ اسورۃ النساء۴) نوت نماز اہم عبادت ہے اور طہارت اس کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اس لئے طہارت کو مقدم کیا۔ اب طہارت کے ابحاث ختم ہونے کے بعد نماز کے مسائل کو شروع کیا وقت وقت نماز کے لئے شرط ہے اگر وقت نہ ہوا ہوتو نماز ہی واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ وقت آنے پر ہی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے۔ وجوب کی اصل وجہ تو اللہ کا حکم ہے لیکن ہم اللہ کے ہر وقت کے حکم کو نہیں سن پاتے اس لئے علامت کے طور پر وقت کو رکھ دیا کہ جب وقت آئے تو سمجھ لوکہ حکم آگیا اور نماز شروع کرو ۔ وقت کی دلیل او پر کی آیت ہے۔ ۱۳۴) (۱) فجر کا اول وقت جب کہ صبح صادق طلوع ہو جائے، فجر ثانی وہ افق میں پھیلی ہوئی سفید روشنی ہے اور فجر کا آخری وقت جب تک کہ سورج طلوع نہ ہو جائے۔
فجر کی نماز فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے وسبح بحمدک ربک قبل طلوع الشمس وقبل غروبها ومن اناء الليل فسبح واطرافها النهار لعلک ترضی (ب) ( آیت ۱۳۰ سوره طه ۲۰) بلکہ اس آیت میں تمام نمازوں کے اوقت کی طرف اشارہ ہو گیا۔ اور نماز فجر کے وقت کی طرف بھی اشارہ ہو گیا۔ الفجر الثاني : فجر کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) صبح کاذب (۲) صبح صادق ۔ صبح کاذب : مشرقی افق میں پھیڑے کی دم کی طرح لمبی سی روشنی ہوتی ہے جو بہت مشکل سے نظر آتی ہے۔ اس کے تھوڑی دیر کے بعد محرابی شکل میں پھیلی ہوئی روشنی ہوتی ہے جس کو صبح صادق کہتے ہیں۔ بعض ماہرین فلکیات اس کو اٹھارہ ڈگری پر بتاتے ہیں اور بعض پندرہ ڈگری پر بتاتے ہیں۔ دلائل دونوں طرف ہیں۔ اسی صبح صادق کے وقت فجر کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اسی کی طرف مصنف نے البیاض المعترض کہکر اشارہ کیا ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کی دلیل یہ ہے عن سمرة بن جندب قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يغرنكم اذان بلال ولا هذا البياض لعمود الصبح حتى يستطير هكذا (ج) (مسلم شریف، باب بیان ان الدخول في الصوم تحصل بطلوع الفجر، کتاب الصوم ص ۳۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۹۴) حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ روشنی جو لمبائی میں ہو وہ صبح صادق نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یستطیر یعنی افق میں پھیلی ہوئی روشنی صبح صادق ہے۔ آیت میں بھی اس طرف اشارہ ہے وكلوا واشربوا حتى
حاشیہ : (الف) نماز مؤمن پر وقت متعینہ کے ساتھ فرض ہے (ب) اپنے رب کی تسبیح بیان کیجئے سورج کے طلوع ہونے سے پہلے اور غروب سے پہلے اور رت کے کچھ حصے میں ۔ پس تسبیح بیان کیجئے اور دن کے کناروں میں شاید کہ آپ راضی ہو جا ئیں (ج) آپ کو دھو کے میں نہ ڈالے بلال کی اذان اور نہ یہ صبح کی لمبی سفیدی یہاں تک کہ روشنی پھیل نہ جائے۔
Book of Prayer. Important note: The lexical meaning of salah is supplication. In Shariah, the prescribed actions (arkan) are called salah. The proof for the obligation of salah is many verses of the Quran, e.g. 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers a decree of specified times' (Surah an-Nisa 4:103). Note: Prayer is an important worship and purification is its condition. Therefore, purification was presented first. Now, after completing the discussions on purification, the issues of prayer are started. Time is a condition for prayer; if the time has not come, prayer is not obligatory. Obligation arises only with the arrival of time. The basis of obligation is Allah's command, but we cannot hear Allah's command at every time, so time was established as a sign: when time comes, understand that the command has come and begin prayer. The proof for time is the verse mentioned. (134) (1) The beginning time of Fajr is when the second dawn (subh sadiq) appears, which is the whiteness spreading across the horizon. The end time of Fajr is until sunrise. The proof for the obligation of Fajr prayer is this verse: 'And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting, and during periods of the night [exalt Him] and at the ends of the day, that you may be satisfied' (Surah Taha 20:130). Rather, this verse indicates the times of all prayers, and specifically indicates the time of Fajr prayer. The second dawn: There are two types of dawn: (1) false dawn (subh kazib) and (2) true dawn (subh sadiq). False dawn: a long, tail-like whiteness in the eastern horizon that is very difficult to see. After a short while, a spread-out, arch-shaped whiteness appears, which is called subh sadiq. Some astronomers say it is at 18 degrees, others say at 15 degrees; there are proofs for both. At the time of subh sadiq, Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. The author alluded to this by saying 'al-bayad al-mu'tarid' (the whiteness spreading). The proof from hadith is from Samurah ibn Jundub: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Let not the adhan of Bilal nor this whiteness that appears like a pillar fool you until it spreads out like this.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Sawm, hadith 1094). From the hadith, it is understood that the light that is elongated is not subh sadiq; rather, the light that spreads out (yastatir) across the horizon is subh sadiq. The Quran also alludes to this: 'And eat and drink until' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187). Footnotes: (a) Prayer is prescribed for the believers at fixed times. (b) Exalt with praise of your Lord before sunrise and before sunset, and in the hours of the night, and at the ends of the day, that you may be pleased. (c) Do not let the adhan of Bilal nor this vertical whiteness of dawn fool you until it spreads out like this.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Prayer and first addresses the time of Fajr prayer. The author first gives an important note on the nature of salah and its obligation. Then he states that time is a condition for prayer; the proof is from Quran. Then he specifies that the beginning time of Fajr is the appearance of subh sadiq, which is the whiteness spreading across the horizon, and the end time is sunrise. He distinguishes between false dawn (subh kazib) and true dawn (subh sadiq). False dawn is a vertical light that rises like a wolf's tail, while true dawn is horizontal and spreads. He cites Quranic verse 20:130 as a proof for the times of prayers, especially Fajr. Then he provides the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub that emphasizes that the true dawn is the spreading light, not the pillar-like light. This is crucial for determining the correct time for Fajr prayer and the start of fasting (Sawm). The author also mentions that astronomers differ on the precise angle, but both opinions are considered valid within the school. The Hanafi position is that Fajr time begins when the true dawn appears, and prayer is valid from that moment. The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and is used as evidence.

Key Terms
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): The true dawn: a horizontal, spreading whiteness on the horizon that signals the start of Fajr time.
صبح كاذب (subh kazib): The false dawn: a vertical, tail-like light that appears briefly and then disappears.
البياض المعترض (al-bayad al-mu'tarid): The whiteness that spreads horizontally across the horizon; synonym for subh sadiq.
يستطير (yastatir): Spreads out; used in the hadith to describe the true dawn's appearance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following describes the true dawn (subh sadiq) according to the Hanafi school?
A) A vertical light like a wolf's tail
B) A horizontal spreading light across the horizon
C) A light that disappears quickly
D) A light visible only briefly at dawn

Key Takeaway
Fajr time begins with subh sadiq – the horizontal spreading light – and ends at sunrise; this is established by Quran and authentic hadith.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Time of Fajr Prayer
Ruling with proof defining Fajr prayer times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end of Fajr prayer time according to the Hanafi school and explain the distinction between true and false dawn, citing the proofs.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins at true dawn (horizontal white light) and ends at sunrise — a condition for the obligatory prayer.

This lesson establishes the precise timing for Fajr prayer, a foundational condition for its validity. We will examine the textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that defines the start and end of Fajr, and clarify the important distinction between the true dawn (subh sadiq) and the false dawn (subh kadhib). Understanding this distinction ensures that the prayer is performed within its prescribed time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the time of Fajr prayer. It states that the first time is the appearance of the second dawn (true dawn) and the last time is sunrise.
The time is a condition (shart) for the obligation of prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub (Muslim) which distinguishes between vertical whiteness (false dawn) and spreading whiteness (true dawn). Also references Quranic verses (Surah Taha 20:130, Surah al-Baqarah 2:187).
The hadith is ahad but relied upon for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that the vertical light ('this vertical whiteness of dawn') is not the start, but the spreading light is. The verse about white and black threads also indicates clear distinctness.
This establishes that horizontal spreading light marks true dawn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among the madhahib on the beginning and end of Fajr time, though there is variation in the astronomical calculation of the sun's angle for true dawn.
The Hanafi position is unanimous.

ضروری نوٹ صلوۃ کے لغوی معنی دعا ہے۔ شریعت میں ارکان معہودہ کو صلوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ صلوۃ کے فرض ہونی کی دلیل قرآن کی بہت سی آمیتیں ہیں ۔ مثلا ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا (آیت ۰۳ اسورۃ النساء۴) نوت نماز اہم عبادت ہے اور طہارت اس کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اس لئے طہارت کو مقدم کیا۔ اب طہارت کے ابحاث ختم ہونے کے بعد نماز کے مسائل کو شروع کیا وقت وقت نماز کے لئے شرط ہے اگر وقت نہ ہوا ہوتو نماز ہی واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ وقت آنے پر ہی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے۔ وجوب کی اصل وجہ تو اللہ کا حکم ہے لیکن ہم اللہ کے ہر وقت کے حکم کو نہیں سن پاتے اس لئے علامت کے طور پر وقت کو رکھ دیا کہ جب وقت آئے تو سمجھ لوکہ حکم آگیا اور نماز شروع کرو ۔ وقت کی دلیل او پر کی آیت ہے۔ ۱۳۴) (۱) فجر کا اول وقت جب کہ صبح صادق طلوع ہو جائے، فجر ثانی وہ افق میں پھیلی ہوئی سفید روشنی ہے اور فجر کا آخری وقت جب تک کہ سورج طلوع نہ ہو جائے۔
فجر کی نماز فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے وسبح بحمدک ربک قبل طلوع الشمس وقبل غروبها ومن اناء الليل فسبح واطرافها النهار لعلک ترضی (آیت ۱۳۰ سوره طه ۲۰) بلکہ اس آیت میں تمام نمازوں کے اوقت کی طرف اشارہ ہو گیا۔ اور نماز فجر کے وقت کی طرف بھی اشارہ ہو گیا۔ الفجر الثاني : فجر کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) صبح کاذب (۲) صبح صادق ۔ صبح کاذب : مشرقی افق میں پھیڑے کی دم کی طرح لمبی سی روشنی ہوتی ہے جو بہت مشکل سے نظر آتی ہے۔ اس کے تھوڑی دیر کے بعد محرابی شکل میں پھیلی ہوئی روشنی ہوتی ہے جس کو صبح صادق کہتے ہیں۔ بعض ماہرین فلکیات اس کو اٹھارہ ڈگری پر بتاتے ہیں اور بعض پندرہ ڈگری پر بتاتے ہیں۔ دلائل دونوں طرف ہیں۔ اسی صبح صادق کے وقت فجر کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اسی کی طرف مصنف نے البیاض المعترض کہکر اشارہ کیا ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کی دلیل یہ ہے عن سمرة بن جندب قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يغرنكم اذان بلال ولا هذا البياض لعمود الصبح حتى يستطير هكذا (مسلم شریف، باب بیان ان الدخول في الصوم تحصل بطلوع الفجر، کتاب الصوم ص ۳۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۹۴) حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ روشنی جو لمبائی میں ہو وہ صبح صادق نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یستطیر یعنی افق میں پھیلی ہوئی روشنی صبح صادق ہے۔ آیت میں بھی اس طرف اشارہ ہے وكلوا واشربوا حتى يتبين لكم الخيط الابيض من الخيط الاسود من الفجر (آیت ۱۸۷ سورة البقرة ٢) تبین سے مراد فجر کا خوب واضح ہونا ہے جو صبح صادق کے وقت ہوتا ہے۔
Book of Prayer. [134] (1) The first time of Fajr is when the second dawn appears, which is the whiteness spread across the horizon, and its last time is as long as the sun has not risen. Essential note: The lexical meaning of salah is supplication. In Shariah, the prescribed acts are called salah. The proof of the obligation of salah is many verses of the Quran, e.g., 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at prescribed times' (Surah an-Nisa, verse 103). Note: Prayer is an important worship and purification is a condition for it. Therefore, purification was presented first. Now after the discussion of purification ends, the issues of prayer begin. Time is a condition for prayer; if time has not come, prayer is not even obligatory. It becomes obligatory only when the time comes. The actual cause of obligation is the command of Allah, but we do not hear every command of Allah at all times; therefore time was placed as a sign so that when the time comes, we understand that the command has come and we begin prayer. The proof of time is the above verse. [134] (1) The first time of Fajr is when true dawn (subh sadiq) appears; the second dawn is the white light spread across the horizon, and the last time of Fajr is as long as the sun has not risen. The proof of the obligation of Fajr prayer is this verse: 'And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting...' (Surah Taha, verse 130) Rather, this verse indicates all prayer times and also indicates the time of Fajr prayer. The second dawn: There are two types of dawn: (1) false dawn (subh kadhib) (2) true dawn (subh sadiq). False dawn: In the eastern horizon there is a long, tail-like light like that of a fox, which is very difficult to see. Shortly after it, there is an arched expanding light called true dawn. Some astronomers say it is at 18 degrees, some at 15 degrees; there are proofs on both sides. At the time of this true dawn, Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. The author indicated this by saying 'the whiteness spread across'. The proof in hadith is: Samurah ibn Jundub reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal nor this vertical whiteness of dawn deceive you until it spreads out like this.' (Muslim) The hadith shows that the light that is vertical is not true dawn; rather, the light that spreads across the horizon is true dawn. The verse also indicates this: 'And eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 187). 'Distinct' here means the clear appearance of dawn which occurs at the time of true dawn.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the time of Fajr prayer. The author begins by stating the matn: the first time of Fajr begins with the appearance of the second dawn (fajr sani), which is the whiteness that spreads horizontally across the eastern horizon. This is known as the true dawn (subh sadiq), as opposed to the false dawn (subh kadhib) which appears as a vertical pillar of light. The last time of Fajr is just before sunrise. The commentator then provides context: salah linguistically means supplication, but in Shariah it refers to the specific acts of worship. Its obligation is established by the Quran (Surah an-Nisa 4:103). Purification is a prerequisite, so the book on purification preceded this section. Time is a condition (shart) for prayer; without the entry of time, prayer is not obligatory. The rationale is that Allah's command is signaled by the arrival of time. The proof for the specific timing of Fajr includes the verse from Surah Taha 20:130, which commands glorification before sunrise and before sunset, indicating Fajr and Asr. Also, the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub clarifies that the false dawn is vertical, while the true dawn is horizontal and spreading. The verse from Surah al-Baqarah 2:187 about the white and black threads also refers to the distinctness of true dawn. Thus, the ruling is clear: Fajr time begins at true dawn and ends at sunrise. The Hanafi position is that this is the correct timing, and it is agreed upon by all schools.

Key Terms
الفجر الثاني (al-fajr al-thani): The second dawn, i.e., the true dawn (subh sadiq) which appears as horizontal whiteness on the horizon.
البياض المعترض (al-bayad al-mu'tarid): The whiteness that spreads across the horizon, characteristic of true dawn.
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): The true dawn when the light spreads horizontally, marking the beginning of Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the last time for Fajr prayer according to this passage?
A) Until the sun rises
B) Until the sun reaches its zenith
C) Until the shadow of an object equals its height

Key Takeaway
Fajr time is defined by the spreading horizontal light of true dawn, not the vertical false dawn.

Zuhr Prayer Time: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time of Zuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on Zuhr end time and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including their respective proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Zuhr time extends until shadow is twice the object's height (Abu Hanifa) vs. one shadow (Sahibayn) — a difference in hadith interpretation.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer. While all agree that Zuhr begins immediately after zawal (sun's decline), Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on when Zuhr ends and Asr begins. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi school's ruling on prayer timings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed point
Notice that both sides agree Zuhr begins at zawal. The disagreement is only on the end time.
Zawal is the moment the sun passes the meridian, determined by the sun's movement, not shadows.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: Zuhr time lasts until any object's shadow (excluding zenith shadow) is twice its height. Sahibayn (and most other imams): Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object's height.
The zenith shadow (fay' al-zawal) is always subtracted from measurements.
3
Analyze each proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Abu Dharr where the Prophet delayed Zuhr until shadows were visible on hills — indicating prayer after one shadow is valid, so time extends to two shadows. The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Jibril where on the second day, Jibril prayed Zuhr at one shadow and Asr at two shadows.
Both hadith are ahad, so the evidence is zanni; this explains the ikhtilaf.
4
Note the Hanafi response
The commentator does not reject the Sahibayn's proof but implies Abu Hanifa's view is stronger because the Prophet's delay shows permissibility beyond one shadow. The hadith of Jibril may indicate the optimal time rather than the end of Zuhr.
In Hanafi usul, the qawi (stronger) evidence is preferred when both are zanni.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, a person who prays Zuhr between one and two shadows is valid. According to the Sahibayn, Zuhr time would have ended, so the prayer would be considered qada (make-up). The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view.
This difference affects daily prayer timetables used by Hanafis.

Source Text

[۱۳۵) (۲) واول وقت الظهر اذا زالت الشمس وآخر وقتها عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى اذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه سوى فيء الزوال وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله اذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله سوى فيء الزوال
ظہر کا اول وقت زوال کے فورا بعد سے شروع ہوتا ہے۔ اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اس کے آخری وقت کے بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے یہ ہے کہ سایہ اصلی کے علاوہ دو مثل تک رہتا ہے۔ اور اس کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي ذر قال كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سفر فاراد المؤذن ان يؤذن للظهر فقال النبي الله ابرد، ثم اراد ان يؤذن فقال له ابرد ، حتى رأينا في التلول فقال النبي الا الله ان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم فاذا اشتد الحر فابردوا بالصلوة (بخاری شریف، باب الابراد بالظهر في السفر ص ۷ ۷ے نمبر ۵۳۹) ٹیلہ پستہ قد ہوتا ہے اس کا سایہ نیچے نظر نے لگے یہ اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جب ہر چیز کا سایہ ایک مثل سے زیادہ ہو چکا ہو۔ اس سے اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز ایک مثل کے بعد پڑھی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے ظہر کا وقت دومشل تک ہے فائدہ صاحبین اور دوسرے ائمہ سایہ اصلی کے علاوہ ایک مثل تک ظہر کا وقت کہتے ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اخبرني ابن عباس ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين فصلى الظهر في الاولى منهما حين - الفيء مثل الشراك ثم صلى العصر حين كان كل شيء مثل ظله ثم صلى المغرب حين وجبت الشمس وافطر الصائم ثم صلى العشاء حين غاب الشفق ثم صلى الفجر حين برق الفجر وحرم الطعام على الصائم وصلى المرة الثانية الظهر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثله لوقت العصر بالامس ثم صلى العصر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثليه ثم صلى المغرب لوقته الاول ثم صلى العشاء الآخرة حين ذهب ثلث الليل ثم صلى الصبح حين اسفرت الارض ثم التـفـت الـى جـبـرئيــل فـقـال يـا مـحـمـد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين (ترمذی)
[135] (2) And the first time of Zuhr is when the sun has declined, and its last time according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length excluding the shadow at zenith, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: when the shadow of everything becomes its own length excluding the shadow at zenith. The first time of Zuhr begins immediately after zawal; there is no disagreement about this. However, regarding its last time, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that it lasts until two times the original shadow (excluding the zenith shadow), and after that the time of Asr begins. His evidence is the hadith of Abu Dharr: 'We were with the Messenger of Allah on a journey, and the mu'adhdhin wanted to call the adhan for Zuhr, but the Prophet said, 'Wait for it to cool down.' Then he wanted to call the adhan, and he said, 'Wait for it to cool down,' until we saw the shadows of the hills [lengthen]. Then the Prophet said, 'Indeed, the intensity of heat is from the exhalation of Hell, so when the heat is intense, delay the prayer until it cools down.' (Bukhari) A hill is low; its shadow appears downwards. This can only happen when the shadow of everything has exceeded one time the height. From this, it is understood that Zuhr prayer was offered after one shadow. Therefore, Zuhr time extends to two shadows. Benefit: The Sahibayn and other imams say that Zuhr time lasts until one shadow excluding the zenith shadow. Their evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Jibril led me in prayer twice near the House. In the first time, he prayed Zuhr when the shadow was like the strap of a sandal, then Asr when everything's shadow was its own length, then Maghrib when the sun set, then Isha when the twilight disappeared, then Fajr when dawn broke. In the second time, he prayed Zuhr when the shadow of everything was its own length, which was Asr time the previous day, then Asr when every shadow was twice its length, then Maghrib at its first time, then Isha when one-third of the night had passed, then Fajr when the earth was bright. Then he turned to Jibril and said, 'O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times.' (Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer. All agree that Zuhr begins immediately after zawal (the sun's passing its zenith). The dispute concerns when Zuhr ends and Asr begins. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Zuhr time extends until the shadow of any object (excluding the shadow at zenith) reaches twice the object's height. After that, Asr time begins. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object's height (excluding zenith shadow). Each position is supported by hadith. Abu Hanifa's evidence is the hadith of Abu Dharr where the Prophet delayed Zuhr until the shadows of hills were visible, indicating that after one shadow length, Zuhr was still valid. The commentator infers that delaying until one shadow is permissible, so the time extends to two shadows. The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Jibril (Gabriel) where in the second day, Jibril prayed Zuhr when each thing's shadow was its own length, and then Asr when each shadow was twice its length, implying that Zuhr ends at one shadow. The Hanafi school generally follows Abu Hanifa's view, though the Sahibayn's view is also transmitted. The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is Abu Hanifa's, as stated in the text.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline westward. It is the beginning of Zuhr time.
مثلين (mithlayn): Two times the length of the object's height (excluding the shadow at zenith). Used to define the end of Zuhr time according to Abu Hanifa.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The shadow of an object at the moment the sun is at its zenith, which is minimal and excluded from shadow calculations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the last time for Zuhr prayer in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) When the shadow of everything becomes twice its length (excluding zenith shadow)
B) When the shadow of everything becomes equal to its length (excluding zenith shadow)
C) When the sun sets
D) When the twilight disappears

Key Takeaway
Zuhr prayer time in the Hanafi school extends until the shadow is twice the object's height (excluding zenith shadow), based on the relied-upon view of Abu Hanifa.

Times for Zuhr and Asr: The Intra-Hanafi Mithl Dispute
Ruling on Zuhr and Asr times with intra-Hanafi dispute on Asr start

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the end time of Zuhr and the start time of Asr, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the measure of mithl.

Core Idea
Zuhr ends and Asr begins when the shadow equals its height – but Abu Hanifa says at two mithl, Sahibayn at one.

This lesson examines the precise times for Zuhr and Asr prayers according to the Hanafi school. While the end of Zuhr and start of Asr are linked to the length of shadows, there is an important difference of opinion within the school itself. The passage presents the ruling, the evidence, and clarifies which position is relied upon for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what is being ruled upon: the end time of Zuhr and the beginning time of Asr. The base text states that the time of Zuhr ends when the shadow of everything equals its height (one mithl) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn).
The matn cites 'Yusuf and Muhammad' indicating the view of the Sahibayn.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Identify the evidence cited: the hadith of Jibril teaching the prayer times and the hadith of Abu Huraira on catching a rak'ah before sunset. The hadith of Jibril states that the last time of Zuhr is one mithl, and after that Asr begins.
The hadith of Jibril is narrated in Abu Dawud and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit mention of 'one mithl' indicates the boundary between Zuhr and Asr times.
The hadith text: 'The time of Zuhr is from when the sun passes the zenith until the shadow of a man is equal to his height.'
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr time extends until the shadow becomes twice the height (two mithl). The Sahibayn hold one mithl. The text explains this divergence and mentions the concept of 'waqt muhmal' (vacant time) which some scholars proposed but the author rejects.
Abu Hanifa's view is based on a different hadith reading? The text does not specify his dalil.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which view is mufta bihi. The commentary states that the Sahibayn's view is supported by the hadith and that caution dictates not praying Zuhr after one mithl nor Asr before two mithl, but the relied-upon position is that Asr begins at one mithl.
Later practice follows the Sahibayn due to the strength of the hadith evidence.

۱۳۹ (۳) عصر کا اول وقت جب کہ ظہر کا وقت نکل جائے دونوں قول پر۔ اور اس کا آخری وقت جب تک سورج غروب نہ ہو جائے۔ ر صاحبین کے قول کے مطابق مثل اول کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق دومشل کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا۔ اور بعض ائمہ نے دونوں حدیثوں کو دیکھتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ ایک مثل کے بعد اور دومثل سے پہلے وقت مہمل ہے یعنی نہ ظہر کا وقت ہے اور نہ عصر کا وقت ہے۔
نوت احادیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ ظہر کے بعد فورا عصر کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے نہ دونوں کے درمیان وقت مہمل ہے اور نہ مشترک ہے۔ پہلی حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عصر کی آخری نماز دوشل پر پڑھی گئی لیکن دوسری حدیث میں موجود ہے کہ غروب آفتاب تک عصر کا وقت موجود ہے۔ البته آفتاب زرد ہونے کے بعد نماز مکروہ ہونے لگتی ہے۔ اس لئے آفتاب زرد ہونے سے پہلے عصر کی نماز پڑھنی چاہئے ۔ تا ہم غروب سے پہلے

سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے تک ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان النبی الا الله قال من ادرك من الصبح ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرك الصبح و من ادرك من العصر ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرك العصر (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن ادرک رکعتة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس ص ۲۵ نمبر ۶ ۱۸ بخاری شریف ، باب من ادرک من الفجر ركعته ص
