Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) [say]: when the shadow of everything becomes like it [16] (3) And the beginning time of Asr is when the time of Zuhr exits according to the two sayings, and its last time is as long as the sun has not set. Chapter: What has come regarding the prayer times from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Sahih? Book of prayer no. 149, Abu Dawud, Book of times, p. 62 no. (1393). In this hadith all prayer times are mentioned. And the last time of Zuhr is stated as one mithl. And after one mithl the time of Asr begins. Based on this hadith, the Sahibayn also went that the time of Zuhr remains until one mithl. However, caution is that one should not pray Zuhr after one mithl and should not pray Asr before two mithl. Lexicon: at zawal: exactly at midday when the sun is overhead, the slight shadow that occurs is called 'original shadow' and 'fi al-zawal'. Leaving that aside, when the shadow of everything becomes equal to its height, that is called one mithl shadow. For example, a man's height is five and a half feet. So besides the original shadow, if the shadow extends to five and a half feet, that is one mithl. And besides the original shadow, if the shadow extends to eleven feet, that becomes two mithl. 139 (3) The beginning time of Asr is when the time of Zuhr exits according to both sayings. And its last time is as long as the sun has not set. According to the Sahibayn's saying, after the first mithl, Asr time begins. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying, after the second mithl, Asr time begins. And some imams, looking at both hadith, said that after one mithl and before two mithl the time is vacant (muhmal), i.e., it is neither Zuhr time nor Asr time. Note: From hadith it is clear that immediately after Zuhr, Asr time begins, there is neither vacant time nor shared time between them. The first hadith shows that the last Asr prayer was prayed at two mithl, but the second hadith states that the time of Asr exists until sunset. However, after the sun becomes yellow, prayer becomes disliked. So Asr should be prayed before the sun becomes yellow. Nevertheless, if one prays Asr before sunset, it will be ada (on time), not qada, because the time still remains. Evidence for Asr time continuing until sunset: (1) 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting' (Surah Taha 20:130). The meaning of 'before its setting' is that the time of Asr lasts until before the sun sets. (2) In a hadith: from Abu Huraira that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on who catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets, p. 25 no. 618; Bukhari, chapter on who catches one rak'ah of Fajr...). Footnote: (continued from previous page) Then he led the last Isha prayer when one-third of the night had passed. Then he led the Fajr prayer when the earth became light. Then Jibril turned to me and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the prayer times are between these two times. (a) He (peace be upon him) said: Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has indeed caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has indeed caught Asr.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence on the times for Zuhr and Asr prayers. The matn (base text) states that the end of Zuhr time is when the shadow of everything becomes equal to its height (one mithl) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) — this is one view. The beginning of Asr is when Zuhr time ends, so after one mithl. The last time of Asr is until sunset. The commentary explains that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that Zuhr time ends at one mithl, so Asr begins then. Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr time ends at two mithl, so Asr begins after two mithl. The term 'mithl' means the length of the shadow beyond the original midday shadow. The passage also discusses the concept of 'waqt muhmal' — a vacant time between one and two mithl — which some scholars proposed, but the author rejects it, affirming that Zuhr and Asr times are consecutive with no gap, based on hadith. Evidence for Asr's last time is provided from the Quran (Surah Taha 20:130) and a hadith from Abu Huraira (whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr). The footnote recounts the hadith of Jibril teaching the prayer times, emphasizing that the times are between the two extremes.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): The length of the shadow of an object equal to its own height, excluding the original shadow at midday (zawal).
وقت مہمل (waqt muhmal): A time interval that is considered vacant, i.e., not belonging to any prayer, occurring between one and two mithl according to some scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does the time of Asr begin?
A) When the sun reaches its zenith
B) When the shadow of everything becomes equal to its height (one mithl) after midday
C) When the shadow becomes twice the height (two mithl)
D) At sunset

Key Takeaway
Zuhr ends and Asr begins when the shadow equals the object's height (one mithl) per the relied-upon Hanafi view, but there is a valid ikhtilaf; caution may lead to delaying Asr, but the mufta bihi is one mithl.

Time of Maghrib and the Definition of Shafaq
Ruling on Maghrib time and intra-Hanafi dispute on shafaq definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Maghrib time, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on shafaq, and identify the evidence used by Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of shafaq; the dispute is whether shafaq is redness or white glow.

The time of Maghrib prayer is fixed from sunset until the disappearance of shafaq (twilight). However, the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on what exactly shafaq means: is it the redness in the sky after sunset, or the white glow that follows? This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Maghrib is a fard prayer. Its time begins at sunset and ends when shafaq disappears. Note that 'shafaq' is ambiguous.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'When you pray Maghrib, its time is until the shafaq falls' is the primary textual evidence. Also the hadith of Abu Mas'ud and the athar of Umar bin Abdul Aziz.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative term is 'shafaq'. The evidence does not specify its meaning, leading to different interpretations.
The ambiguity allows for multiple legal readings.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa: shafaq is the white glow after redness. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): shafaq is the redness itself.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentary favors Abu Hanifa's view by providing additional evidence: analogy with Fajr (white outstretched), and the practice of praying Isha after the horizon becomes dark (implying whiteness is still Maghrib time).
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's definition (white glow).

۱۳۷ (۲) واول وقـت الـمـغـرب اذا غربت الشمــس وآخر وقتها مالم تغب الشفق [۱۳۸ (۵) وهو البياض الذى يرى في الافق بعد الحمرة عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله هو الحمرة.
[۱۳۷] (۴) مغرب کا اول و تجب سورج ڈوب جائے اور اس کا آخر وقت جب تک کہ شفق غائب نہ ہو جائے۔ مغرب کے اول وقت کے بارے میں حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ اور حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام نے مغرب کی نماز دونوں دن سورج غروب ہونے کے بعد ہی پڑھائی۔ اس لئے کہ مستحب وقت وہی ہے۔ لیکن مغرب کا آخری وقت حقیقت میں شفق کے غروب ہونے تک ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن عمران النبی الا الله قال اذا صليتم الفجر ... فاذا صليتم المغرب فانه وقت الى اين يسقط الشفق (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب اوقات الصلوات ائمس ص ۲۲۲ نمبر ۶۱۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی مواقیت الصلواۃ ص ۴۰ نمبر (۱۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کا وقت شفق کے غروب ہونے تک رہتا ہے۔
[۱۳۸ (۵) شفق وہ سفید روشنی ہے جو افق میں سرخی کے بعد دیکھی جاتی ہے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا شفق وہ سرخی ہے۔ فتاب ڈوبنے کے بعد پہلے سرخی آتی ہے پھر سفید روشنی پھیلی ہوئی ہوتی ہے۔ پھر سفید روشنی لمبی سی ہوتی ہے جس کو بیاض مستطیر اور پھر بیاض مستطیل کہتے ہیں۔ اس کے بعد افق پر مکمل اندھیرا چھا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک سرخی کے بعد جو بیاض مستطیر ہوتی ہے وہاں تک مغرب کا وقت ہے۔ اس کے بعد عشا کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے (۱) فجر میں بیاض مستطیر فجر کا وقت ہے۔ اسی طرح بیاض مستطیر مغرب کا وقت ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ دونوں ایک ہی طرح ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے سمعت ابا مسعود الانصارى يقول ... ويصلي المغرب حين تسقط الشمس ويصلـى العشاء حين يسود الافق وربما اخرها حتى يجتمع الناس (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی المواقیت ص ۶۲ ۶۳ نمبر ۳۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ عشا کی نماز افق کالا ہونے کے بعد پڑھا کرتے تھے ۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیاض مستطیر تک مغرب کا وقت ہے۔ جو سرخی کے بعد آتی ہے۔ کیونکہ افق کالاسفیدی غائب ہونے کے بعد ہی ہوگا۔ اس کی تائید اس اثر سے ہوتی ہے۔ کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز ان صلوا صلوة العشاء اذا ذهب بياض الافق فيما بينكم و بين ثلث الليل (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وقت العشاء الاخرة ص ۵۵۶، نمبر ۲۱۱۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ افق کے بیاض جانے یعنی شفق ابیض کے ڈوبنے کے بعد نماز عشاء کا وقت ہوتا ہے۔
137 (2) And the beginning time of Maghrib is when the sun sets, and its last time is as long as the twilight (shafaq) has not disappeared. [138 (5) It is the white glow that is seen in the horizon after the redness according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said it is the redness. [137] (4) The beginning time of Maghrib is when the sun sets, and its last time is until the shafaq disappears. The hadith about the beginning time of Maghrib has passed. And Jibril (peace be upon him) led the Maghrib prayer on both days after sunset. Therefore, the preferred time is that. But the last time of Maghrib is actually until the shafaq disappears. The evidence for this is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar? that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you pray Fajr... and when you pray Maghrib, its time is until the shafaq falls.' (Muslim, chapter on prayer times, p. 222 no. 612; Tirmidhi, chapter on prayer times, p. 40 no. 15). From this hadith it is known that the time of Maghrib remains until the shafaq disappears. [138 (5) Shafaq is the white light that is seen in the horizon after the redness according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said it is the redness. After sunset, first redness appears, then a white glow spreads. Then the white glow becomes elongated, called 'white outstretched' (bayad mustatir) and then 'white elongated' (bayad mustatil). After that, complete darkness covers the horizon. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, until the white outstretched (bayad mustatir) that comes after the redness, that is the time of Maghrib. After that, the time of Isha begins. (1) In Fajr, the white outstretched is the time of Fajr. Similarly, the white outstretched should be the time of Maghrib, because both are alike. (2) In a hadith: I heard Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari say... he would pray Maghrib when the sun set, and pray Isha when the horizon became dark, and sometimes he would delay it until people gathered. (Abu Dawud, chapter on times, p. 62-63 no. 394). In this hadith, he would pray Isha after the horizon became dark. This means that the time of Maghrib is until the white outstretched (which comes after redness), because the horizon becomes dark only after the whiteness disappears. This is supported by the athar: Umar ibn Abdul Aziz wrote: 'Pray the Isha prayer when the whiteness of the horizon disappears, between you and one-third of the night.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on time of Isha, p. 556 no. 2110). From this athar, it is understood that the time of Isha is after the whiteness of the horizon (i.e., white shafaq) disappears.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the time of Maghrib and an intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shafaq (twilight). The matn states: The beginning of Maghrib time is sunset, and its end is when shafaq disappears. The commentary explains that shafaq is defined differently: Abu Hanifa says it is the white glow after redness; the Sahibayn say it is the redness itself. Thus, according to Abu Hanifa, Maghrib time extends until the white glow vanishes (which happens after redness), while according to the Sahibayn, it ends when the redness disappears. The author provides evidence: the hadith of Jibril showing Maghrib is prayed right after sunset, and another hadith stating Maghrib time lasts until shafaq falls. Then he gives rational proof: as in Fajr, the white outstretched (bayad mustatir) marks the time of Fajr, so similarly in Maghrib, the white outstretched marks its end. He also cites the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying Isha after the horizon becomes dark, implying that before that, Maghrib time remains. The athar from Umar bin Abdul Aziz confirms that Isha is after the whiteness disappears, supporting Abu Hanifa's view that Maghrib time includes the white glow.

Key Terms
شفق (shafaq): Twilight; the light remaining in the sky after sunset. According to Abu Hanifa, it is the white glow (bayad) after redness; according to the Sahibayn, it is the redness itself.
بیاض مستطیر (bayad mustatir): The spreading white glow on the horizon after sunset, before the elongated white (mustatil) and complete darkness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is shafaq, and when does Maghrib time end?
A) Shafaq is the redness; Maghrib ends when redness disappears
B) Shafaq is the white glow after redness; Maghrib ends when white glow disappears
C) Shafaq is the white glow; Maghrib ends at sunset
D) Shafaq is the darkness; Maghrib ends when it becomes completely dark

Key Takeaway
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of shafaq; in the Hanafi school, shafaq is the white glow after redness (mufta bihi).

Time of Maghrib Prayer: From Sunset to Disappearance of Shafaq
Ruling with proof: time limits of Maghrib prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end times of Maghrib prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Maghrib time begins at sunset and lasts until the shafaq (twilight) disappears.

This lesson establishes the temporal boundaries for Maghrib prayer, a daily obligation. The Hanafi school defines the end of Maghrib by a natural phenomenon—the disappearance of twilight after sunset. Understanding this timeframe is essential for performing the prayer within its valid window, and a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar provides the textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Maghrib prayer, which is wajib. The ruling governs its permissible time window.
Maghrib is a fard prayer, but its time window is wajib to observe.
2
State the beginning time
Maghrib begins when the sun sets (ghurub al-shams). The source states: 'و اول وقت المغرب اذا غربت الشمس'.
The exact moment of sunset is determined by the disappearance of the sun's disk below the horizon.
3
State the ending time
Maghrib ends when the shafaq (twilight) disappears. The source states: 'وآخر وقتها مالم تغب الشفق'.
The definition of shafaq will be discussed in a later lesson; here it is sufficient that the time ends with its disappearance.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When you pray Maghrib, its time is until the shafaq falls.'
This hadith is narrated by Muslim and Tirmidhi, and is considered sahih (authentic).
5
Analyze the proof
The phrase 'وقت إلى أن يسقط الشفق' explicitly indicates that the time continues until the shafaq falls, establishing the endpoint.
The hadith uses the continuous preposition 'ila' (until), which indicates that the time remains valid up to that point.

And the first time of Maghrib is when the sun sets, and its last time is as long as the shafaq has not disappeared. [137] (4) The first time of Maghrib is when the sun sets, and its last time is until the shafaq disappears. The hadith regarding the first time has passed. And Hadrat Jibril عليه السلام led Maghrib prayer both days after sunset, so that is the recommended time. But the last time of Maghrib in reality is until the disappearance of shafaq. Its proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: When you pray Fajr... and when you pray Maghrib, its time is until the shafaq falls. (Muslim, chapter on prayer times, p.222 no.612; Tirmidhi, chapter on prayer times, p.40 no.15) From this hadith it is known that the time of Maghrib lasts until the shafaq disappears.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Maghrib prayer. The author first states the matn (Arabic line) which is a standard Hanafi ruling: Maghrib begins at sunset and ends when shafaq (twilight) disappears. The Urdu sharh explains that the first time (mustahabb) is immediately after sunset, as demonstrated by Jibril's leading the Prophet in prayer. The last time is until shafaq disappears, proven by the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar. The hadith text is quoted (though the OCR has some corruption). This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon by the Hanafi school, though the definition of shafaq will be discussed in the next lesson.

Key Terms
شفق (shafaq): The twilight after sunset; the text does not define it here but will discuss it in the next lesson.

Isha Prayer Time: From Shafaq to Fajr
Defines Isha prayer time boundaries with textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end times of Isha prayer according to the Hanafi school, and identify the key proofs from hadith and companion statements.

Core Idea
Isha time begins when twilight fades and ends at Fajr, not at midnight.

This passage from Sharh al-Sameri establishes the boundary times for Isha prayer. The beginning is marked by the disappearance of shafaq, while the end is critically extended until Fajr, based on the Prophet's practice and explicit companion statements. This lesson examines the evidence, which is agreed upon by all imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is Isha prayer. Its time is defined as beginning with the disappearance of shafaq and ending at Fajr. This is a ruling on the permissible time window.
The beginning time is assumed from earlier lessons.
2
Analyze the first proof (hadith)
The hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet delayed Isha until late in the night, indicating the time extends well beyond early night. This refutes the idea that it ends shortly after Maghrib.
Muslim, hadith 638.
3
Analyze the second proof (companion statements)
Abu Huraira explicitly said the last time is at the rising of Fajr. ʿAbd al-Rahman ibn ʿAwf ruled that a woman who becomes pure before Fajr prays both Maghrib and Isha, confirming Isha time remains until then.
Bayhaqi, Sunan al-Kubra, 1763.
4
Note the consensus
The text says all imams hold this view, so the ruling is universally accepted (muttafaq alayh).

Source Text

[١٣٩ (٦) واول وقت العشاء اذا غاب الشفق وآخر وقتها ما لم يطلع الفجر

عشا کا اول وقت جب شفق غائب ہو جائے اور اس کا آخر وقت جب تک کہ فجر نہ طلوع ہو جائے۔ عشا کے اول وقت کے بارے میں مسئلہ نمبر ۲ اور مسئلہ نمبرہ میں حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ البتہ آخری وقت کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے عن صلى الله عائشة قالت اعتم النبى لعل الله ذات ليلة حتى ذهب عامة الليل وحتى نام اهل المسجد (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب وقت العشاء وتأخيرها ص ۲۲۹ نمبر ۶۳۸) اس حدیث سے مولوم ہوا کہ عامتہ المیل رات کا ایک بڑا حصہ چلا گیا۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ آدھی رات چلی گئی تھی ۔ اس لئے آدھی رات تک نماز پڑھنے کا ثبوت صحیح حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ اور آخر رات تک عشا کے وقت ہونے کی دلیل صحابہ کا قول ہے قال لابي هريرة ما افرط صلوة العشاء؟ قال طلوع الفجر و عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف في امرأة تطهر قبل طلوع الفجر صلت المغرب والعشاء (ج) (السنن بیھقی، باب آخر وقت الجواز الصلوة العشاء ، ج اول ص ۵۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۶۳) ص صحابی کے اس قول سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشاء کا وقت طلوع فجر سے پہلے تک ہے۔ تمام ائمہ کا یہی مسلک ہے
[139] (6) And the first time of Isha is when shafaq disappears, and its last time is as long as Fajr has not risen. The first time of Isha is when shafaq disappears, and its last time is until Fajr rises. The hadith regarding the first time has passed in issues 2 and 5. However, regarding the last time, this hadith: from Aisha, she said: The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم delayed Isha one night until most of the night had passed and until the people of the mosque slept. (Muslim, chapter on Isha time and delaying it, p.229 no.638) From this hadith it is known that a large portion of the night passed. In another hadith, it is said that half the night passed. Therefore, the proof of praying until half the night is established from a sound hadith. And the proof that Isha time lasts until the end of the night is the statement of the Companions: Abu Huraira was asked, 'When is the last time of Isha?' He said, 'At the rising of Fajr.' And from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf regarding a woman who becomes pure before the rising of Fajr, she prays Maghrib and Isha. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on last time of permissibility of Isha prayer, vol.1 p.553 no.1763) From this statement of a Companion it is known that the time of Isha is until before the rising of Fajr. All imams hold this view.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Isha prayer. The matn states: Isha begins when shafaq disappears and ends at Fajr. The Urdu sharh explains that the beginning time has been covered earlier, so it focuses on the end time. Two proofs are given: (1) The hadith of Aisha that the Prophet delayed Isha until most of the night had passed, indicating that the time extends into the night. (2) The statements of Companions, particularly Abu Huraira stating the last time is at Fajr, and the ruling of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf regarding a woman who becomes pure before Fajr that she should pray both Maghrib and Isha, proving that Isha time remains until Fajr. The commentary notes that all imams agree on this final time. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally accepted.

Key Terms
شفق (shafaq): The twilight after sunset, the marker for the end of Maghrib and the beginning of Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At midnight
B) At the rising of Fajr
C) One hour after sunset
D) When the shafaq appears

Key Takeaway
Isha prayer time is valid from the disappearance of twilight (shafaq) until the break of dawn (Fajr), as established by prophetic practice and companion consensus.

Time of 'Isha Prayer: Beginning with Shafaq, Ending at Fajr
States ruling with proof for 'Isha timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end times of 'Isha prayer according to the Hanafi school, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on shafaq, and cite the proofs from hadith and companion statements.

Core Idea
The time of 'Isha extends from the disappearance of shafaq until Fajr; the definition of shafaq is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage establishes the time boundaries for 'Isha prayer. The author presents the ruling and then provides a series of proofs: a hadith defining shafaq as redness, a hadith showing the Prophet delaying 'Isha until late night, and companion statements declaring that the time lasts until Fajr. Within the Hanafi school, there is an important disagreement on whether shafaq refers to the red or white twilight, influencing when 'Isha actually begins.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
The first time of 'Isha is when shafaq disappears; the last time is before Fajr.
2
Define the shafaq dispute
Note that the Sahibayn (and majority of imams) define shafaq as redness; Abu Hanifa defines it as whiteness.
This affects the actual beginning time in practice.
3
Analyze the hadith for beginning time
The hadith of Ibn Umar states 'al-shafaq al-humrah' – the shafaq is the redness; when it disappears, prayer becomes obligatory. This supports the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the proofs for end time
The hadith of 'Aisha shows the Prophet delayed 'Isha until a large part of the night passed; the companion statements explicitly say until Fajr.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa (shafaq = whiteness), but the text presents the Sahibayn's view as the majority.
Mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view per later tarjih.

Source Text

[١٣٩ (٦) واول وقت العشاء اذا غاب الشفق وآخر وقتها ما لم يطلع الفجر
فائدہ صاحبین اور جمہور ائمہ کے نزدیک بیض مستطیر کے پہلے جو سرخی ہے وہاں تک مغرب کا وقت ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله الله الشفق الحمرة فاذا غاب الشفق وجبت الصلوة (الف) (دار قطنی ، باب في صفة المغرب و المسح ج اول ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۰۴۴ر سفن سیھتی ، باب دخول وقت العشاء بغيبوبته الشفق ، ج اول ص ۵۴۸، نمبر ۱۷۴۴) اس حدیث اور ابو ہریرہ کے قول سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سرخ شفق تک مغرب کا وقت ہے اس کے غروب ہونے کے بعد عشا کا وقت شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔
[۱۳۹] (۶) عشا کا اول وقت جب شفق غائب ہو جائے اور اس کا آخر وقت جب تک کہ فجر نہ طلوع ہو جائے۔ عشا کے اول وقت کے بارے میں مسئلہ نمبر ۲ اور مسئلہ نمبرہ میں حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ البتہ آخری وقت کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے عن صلى الله عائشة قالت اعتم النبى لعل الله ذات ليلة حتى ذهب عامة الليل وحتى نام اهل المسجد (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب وقت العشاء وتأخيرها ص ۲۲۹ نمبر ۶۳۸) اس حدیث سے مولوم ہوا کہ عامتہ المیل رات کا ایک بڑا حصہ چلا گیا۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ آدھی رات چلی گئی تھی ۔ اس لئے آدھی رات تک نماز پڑھنے کا ثبوت صحیح حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ اور آخر رات تک عشا کے وقت ہونے کی دلیل صحابہ کا قول ہے قال لابي هريرة ما افرط صلوة العشاء؟ قال طلوع الفجر و عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف في امرأة تطهر قبل طلوع الفجر صلت المغرب والعشاء (ج) (السنن بیھقی، باب آخر وقت الجواز الصلوة العشاء ، ج اول ص ۵۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۶۳) ص صحابی کے اس قول سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشاء کا وقت طلوع فجر سے پہلے تک ہے۔ تمام ائمہ کا یہی مسلک ہے
خير
[139] (6) And the first time of 'Isha is when the shafaq disappears, and its last time is when dawn does not rise. Benefit: According to the Sahibayn and the majority of imams, the time of Maghrib is until the redness that appears before the white twilight. Their proof is this hadith: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The shafaq is the redness. So when the shafaq disappears, the prayer (of 'Isha) becomes obligatory.' (Al-Daraqutni, chapter on description of Maghrib and wiping, vol. 1, p. 276, no. 1044; Sunan al-Sughra? , chapter on entering the time of 'Isha with the disappearance of shafaq, vol. 1, p. 548, no. 1744). From this hadith and the statement of Abu Hurairah, it is known that Maghrib time lasts until the red shafaq; after it disappears, the time of 'Isha begins. [139] (6) The first time of 'Isha is when the shafaq disappears, and its last time is until dawn does not rise. Regarding the first time of 'Isha, the hadith has already passed in issue no. 2 and issue no. ... However, regarding the last time, there is this hadith: From 'Aisha, she said: 'The Prophet delayed 'Isha one night until a large part of the night had passed and until the people of the mosque had fallen asleep.' (Muslim, chapter on the time of 'Isha and delaying it, p. 229, no. 638). From this hadith it is known that a large part of the night had passed. Another hadith states that half the night had passed. Therefore, the proof that prayer up to midnight is valid is established by authentic hadith. And the proof that the time of 'Isha extends to the end of the night is the statement of the Companions: Abu Hurairah was asked, 'When is the time of 'Isha prayer?' He said: 'At dawn.' And from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf regarding a woman who becomes pure before dawn, he said: 'She will pray Maghrib and 'Isha.' (Al-Bayhaqi, Sunan, chapter on the last permissible time of 'Isha prayer, vol. 1, p. 553, no. 1763). From the statement of this Companion it is known that the time of 'Isha extends until before dawn. All imams hold this view. End.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the beginning and end times of the 'Isha prayer. The author first states the ruling: 'Isha begins when the shafaq (twilight) disappears and ends before Fajr. Then a benefit (fā'idah) explains that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the majority of imams interpret shafaq as redness, so Maghrib ends when the red twilight vanishes. This is supported by a hadith from Ibn Umar where the Prophet defined shafaq as redness. The passage then provides evidence for the last time of 'Isha: a hadith from 'Aisha that the Prophet delayed 'Isha until a large part of the night passed, implying the time extends at least that long. Further, a hadith indicates half the night, and a companion statement from Abu Hurairah and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf shows that 'Isha can be prayed until Fajr. The author concludes that all imams agree on this. Note that within the Hanafi school, there is an ikhtilaf on the definition of shafaq: Abu Hanifa held it is whiteness, while the Sahibayn held it is redness. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is that of Abu Hanifa, but this text presents the Sahibayn's view as an explanation.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): Twilight after sunset; in this context, the Sahibayn define it as redness, Abu Hanifa as whiteness.
الغلس (al-ghalas): The darkness of the last part of the night before dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the time of 'Isha prayer end?
A) At midnight
B) At the appearance of the true dawn (Fajr)
C) At the disappearance of the red twilight
D) When half the night has passed

Key Takeaway
The time for 'Isha prayer begins when the shafaq disappears and ends at the break of true dawn (Fajr), though there is a valid difference on the definition of shafaq.

The Hanafi Recommendation for Isfar in Fajr and the Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on Fajr prayer timing with proofs and reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on isfar for Fajr, state the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response that reconciles both hadiths.

Core Idea
Isfar is recommended to increase the congregation; if people already gather early, ghalas is also acceptable.

This lesson examines a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the preferred time for Fajr prayer. While both agree Fajr begins at true dawn, they differ on whether to pray early (ghalas) or after lightening (isfar). The passage presents the Hanafi ruling with its proof, then the Shafi'i counterproof, and finally the Hanafi reconciliation based on local practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: Isfar is mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah) for Fajr. Note the two reasons: to increase the congregation and the hadith command.
The ruling is not absolute; it is conditioned.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that ghalas (early darkness) is better for Fajr, as it is for all prayers: earliest time is best.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The dalil is the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij: 'Lighten with Fajr, for it is greater in reward.' The imperative indicates recommendation.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
4
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i dalil is the hadith of 'Aisha: women attended Fajr in ghalas and were unrecognizable. This shows the practice of the Prophet.
This hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reconcile: the Prophet's practice in Madinah was that people came early. If the community also comes early (like in Ramadan), ghalas is fine. Otherwise, isfar is better to gather more people.
This shows the Hanafi principle of considering maslahah (public benefit).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب الاسفار بالفجر
فجر میں اسفار کرنا مستحب ہے۔ فجر کا اصل وقت تو طلوع صبح صادق سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ اسفار کر کے فجر کی نماز شروع کرے۔ (۱) جماعت بڑی ہوگی ورنہ لوگ فلس اور اندھیرے میں کم آئیں گے اور جماعت کی قلت ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن رافع بن خديج قال سمعت رسول الله يقول اسفروا بالفجر فانه اعظم للاجور (ب) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب الاسفار بالجرص ۴۰ نمبر ۱۵۴ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی وقت اصبح ص ۶۷ نمبر (۴۲۴) اس میں الفاظ یوں ہیں اصبحوا بالصبح اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فجر کو اسفار کر کے پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔
مانده امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک ہر نماز کو اول وقت میں پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ اور فجر کو غلس اور اندھیرے میں پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عائشة اخبرته قالت كن نساء المؤمنات يشهدن مع رسول الله الله صلوة الفجر متلفعات بمروطهن ثم ينقلن الى بيوتهن حين يقضين الصلوة لا يعرفهن احد من الغلس (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقت الفجر ص ۸۲ نمبر ۵۷۸ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب التبكير با صبح ص۲۳۰ نمبر ۶۴۵) اس حدیث میں دیکھئے غلس میں نماز پڑھی گئی۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مدینہ کی طرح لوگ غلس میں مسجد میں آجاتے ہوں جیسے رمضان میں آجاتے ہیں تو غلس میں مستحب ہے اور اگر لوگ سوئے رہتے ہوں تو اسفار مستحب ہے۔
It is recommended to lighten (isfar) with Fajr. In Fajr, it is mustahabb to perform isfar. The actual time of Fajr begins at true dawn, but it is mustahabb to start Fajr prayer after lightening. (1) The congregation will be larger; otherwise people will come less in darkness and the congregation will be small. (2) In a hadith: From Rafi' ibn Khadij, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Lighten with Fajr, for it is greater in reward.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on isfar with Fajr, p. 40, no. 154; Abu Dawud, chapter on the time of dawn, p. 67, no. 424). In this, the wording is 'asbihu bi al-subh' (make dawn light). From this it is known that it is mustahabb to pray Fajr after lightening. However, Imam Shafi'i and other imams hold that it is mustahabb to pray every prayer at its earliest time, and for Fajr it is mustahabb to pray in ghalas (darkness). Their proof is this hadith: 'Aisha informed him: 'The believing women used to attend Fajr prayer with the Messenger of Allah wrapped in their cloaks; then they would return to their homes after finishing the prayer, and no one would recognize them due to the darkness (ghalas).' (Bukhari, chapter on time of Fajr, p. 82, no. 578; Muslim, chapter on recommendation to hasten Fajr, p. 230, no. 645). Look at this hadith: the prayer was performed in ghalas. We (Hanafis) say: If people come to the mosque in ghalas as in Madinah, like in Ramadan, then ghalas is mustahabb. But if people sleep, then isfar is mustahabb.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the preferred time for Fajr prayer. The author states the Hanafi ruling: isfar (lightening, i.e., delaying until the horizon is bright) is mustahabb. Two reasons: to gather a larger congregation, and a hadith commanding isfar. Then the author presents the Shafi'i position: it is mustahabb to pray Fajr early in deep darkness (ghalas), citing a hadith about women attending in darkness. The Hanafi response reconciles: if people already gather early (like in Madinah), then ghalas is fine; otherwise, isfar is better to ensure a larger congregation. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of considering public benefit (maslahah) and the crowd. The ruling is conditioned on local practice.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): Lightening, i.e., praying Fajr after the horizon has become clearly lightened, not in complete darkness.
الغلس (al-ghalas): The darkness of the last part of the night, just before dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, when is isfar (lightening) recommended for Fajr prayer?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances
B) When people are likely to miss the prayer if it is early
C) Only in winter
D) Never; ghalas is always better

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends isfar for Fajr to maximize congregation, but allows ghalas if people already come early, reconciling both hadiths.

Ibraad: Delaying Zuhr in Summer and Advancing in Winter
Ruling with proof on seasonal Zuhr timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibraad for Zuhr prayer, cite the hadith evidence, and explain the seasonal flexibility.

Core Idea
Zuhr prayer is recommended to be delayed in severe heat and prayed early in winter.

This lesson examines the ruling of ibraad—the recommendation to delay Zuhr prayer in summer until the heat subsides. The passage cites two hadith: one commanding ibraad in intense heat, and another showing the Prophet praying Zuhr immediately at zawal in normal conditions. From these, the Hanafi school derives a flexible approach to Zuhr timing based on season and comfort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the hukm level for ibraad. The passage states it is 'mustahabb' (recommended), which in Hanafi terminology corresponds to sunnah muakkadah.
The imperative 'abirdu' is interpreted as a recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the first from Ibn Umar quoting the Prophet's command to delay when heat is intense; the second from Anas showing the Prophet prayed at zawal in normal conditions.
The first hadith provides the basis for ibraad; the second establishes the default time.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'abirdu' indicates recommendation because it is qualified by a reason ('intense heat is from the blast of Hell'). The Prophet's action at zawal shows permissibility of early prayer in normal conditions.
The reasoning (ta'lil) supports the recommendation, not obligation.
4
Understand the scope
Ibraad applies only when heat is severe (shiddat al-har). In winter, it is recommended to pray early (taqdim). The default is the earliest time, but extreme heat justifies delay.
The ruling is contextual, not absolute.
5
Note cross-madhhab agreement
Most schools agree on ibraad in extreme heat, but the degree of delay may vary. The Hanafi position emphasizes it as a recommended sunnah.
This is a case of ikhtilaf in detail but consensus on the principle.

Source Text

مستحب ہے گرمی میں ظہر کو ٹھنڈا کر کے پڑھنا اور سردی میں اس کو مقدم کرنا۔ (1) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر . . . حدثاه عن رسول الله الا الله انه قال اذا اشتد الحر فابردوا بالصلوه فان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم (د) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الا براد بالظهر في شدة الحرص ۶ نمبر ۳۳ ٫۵ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی تا خیر الظهر في شدة الحرص ۴۰، نمبر ۱۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گرمی ہو تو ظہر کی نماز مؤخر کر کے پڑھنا مستحب ہے (۲) اور حدیث میں ہے انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الله الله خرج حين زاغت الشمس فصلى الظهر (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقت الظهر عن
And cooling down (ibraad) with Zuhr in summer and advancing it in winter. It is mustahabb to delay Zuhr in summer until it cools down and to advance it in winter. (1) In a hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar ... they narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'When the heat is intense, delay the prayer until it cools, for intense heat is from the blast of Hell.' (Bukhari, chapter on cooling down Zuhr in severe heat, p. 6, no. 33?; Tirmidhi, chapter on delaying Zuhr in severe heat, p. 40, no. 157). From this hadith it is known that when it is hot, it is mustahabb to delay Zuhr prayer. (2) And in a hadith: From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah came out when the sun had declined and prayed Zuhr. (Bukhari, chapter on the time of Zuhr, about...)
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the recommended time for Zuhr prayer in different seasons. The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay Zuhr in summer until the heat subsides (ibraad) and to pray it early in winter. Two hadith are cited: one commanding ibraad when heat is severe, explaining it as a mercy to avoid the blast of Hell; the other showing the Prophet prayed Zuhr immediately at decline (zawal) in normal conditions, which applies to winter. This shows flexibility: the default is the earliest time, but extreme heat justifies delay. This is a contextual ruling within the Hanafi school, emphasizing comfort and khushu'.

Key Terms
الإبراد (al-ibraad): Waiting until the heat subsides to pray Zuhr in summer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Recommendation of Isfar for Fajr Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States the Hanafi view on Fajr time and refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on isfar for Fajr, cite the supporting dalil, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi response to a modern congregational scenario.

Core Idea
Fajr at isfar is recommended to increase congregation, but ghalas is acceptable if people already attend early.

The Hanafi school holds that it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay the Fajr prayer until daylight (isfar) rather than praying in the early gloom (ghalas). This lesson examines the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij, the Shafi'i counter-proof from the hadith of 'Aisha, and the Hanafi reconciliation focusing on congregational benefit. Understanding this dispute clarifies a practical difference in Fajr timing across madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling from the matn: it is mustahabb to perform Fajr at isfar. Note that the valid time begins at true dawn, but recommended time is later.
The ruling is only about recommendation, not obligation. Fajr before isfar is still valid.
2
Cite the Hanafi dalil
Quote the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij: 'Asfiru bil-fajr, fa innahu a'zamu lil-ujur.' Explain that the imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a mustahabb ruling.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
State the Shafi'i view: it is mustahabb to pray Fajr at the earliest time (ghalas). Cite their evidence: the hadith of 'Aisha about women leaving in darkness.
The Shafi'is also rely on general principles of hastening to good deeds.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain that the Hanafi response contextualizes the 'Aisha hadith: if the congregation already gathers early (as in Madinah), ghalas is fine; otherwise, isfar is better to increase attendance and reward.
This response uses istihsan and consideration of maslaha (public interest).
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis generally delay Fajr until isfar unless the community habitually comes early; Shafi'is always pray at ghalas.
The difference is in communal practice, not individual validity.

(۸) ويستحب الاسفار بالفجر [ ۱۴۲ (۹) والابراد بالظهر في الصيف وتقديمها في الشتاء.

فجر میں اسفار کرنا مستحب ہے۔ فجر کا اصل وقت تو طلوع صبح صادق سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ اسفار کر کے فجر کی نماز شروع کرے۔ (۱) جماعت بڑی ہوگی ورنہ لوگ فلس اور اندھیرے میں کم آئیں گے اور جماعت کی قلت ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن رافع بن خديج قال سمعت رسول الله يقول اسفروا بالفجر فانه اعظم للاجور (ب) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب الاسفار بالجرص ۴۰ نمبر ۱۵۴ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی وقت اصبح ص ۶۷ نمبر (۴۲۴) اس میں الفاظ یوں ہیں اصبحوا بالصبح اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فجر کو اسفار کر کے پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔

مانده امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک ہر نماز کو اول وقت میں پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ اور فجر کو غلس اور اندھیرے میں پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عائشة اخبرته قالت كن نساء المؤمنات يشهدن مع رسول الله الله صلوة الفجر متلفعات بمروطهن ثم ينقلن الى بيوتهن حين يقضين الصلوة لا يعرفهن احد من الغلس (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقت الفجر ص ۸۲ نمبر ۵۷۸ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب التبكير با صبح ص۲۳۰ نمبر ۶۴۵) اس حدیث میں دیکھئے غلس میں نماز پڑھی گئی۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مدینہ کی طرح لوگ غلس میں مسجد میں آجاتے ہوں جیسے رمضان میں آجاتے ہیں تو غلس میں مستحب ہے اور اگر لوگ سوئے رہتے ہوں تو اسفار مستحب ہے۔
(8) It is recommended to perform the dawn prayer during daylight. [142] (9) And to cool the noon prayer in summer and hasten it in winter. It is recommended to perform Fajr with isfar. The actual time of Fajr begins from the appearance of the true dawn. But it is recommended to start Fajr prayer after isfar. (1) The congregation will be larger; otherwise people will come less in gloom and darkness, and the congregation will be small. (2) There is a hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij: I heard the Messenger of Allah say, 'Perform Fajr at isfar, for it is greater in reward.' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Isfar bil-Fajr, p.40 no.154; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Waqt al-Subh, p.67 no.424) The wording there is 'asbihu bis-subh'. From this, it is understood that performing Fajr at isfar is recommended. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and other imams, it is recommended to pray every prayer at its earliest time, and for Fajr it is recommended to pray in gloom and darkness. Their evidence is the hadith of 'Aisha: 'The believing women used to attend the dawn prayer with the Messenger of Allah wrapped in their cloaks, then they would return to their homes after finishing the prayer, and no one could recognize them due to the darkness.' (Bukhari, Bab Waqt al-Fajr, p.82 no.578; Muslim, Bab Istihbab al-Tabkir bis-Subh, p.230 no.645) In this hadith, the prayer was performed in darkness. We say: If people come to the mosque in darkness like they do in Madinah, as they come in Ramadan, then it is recommended to pray in darkness. But if people remain asleep, then isfar is recommended.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Samarqandi discusses the recommended time for Fajr prayer. The author first states the ruling from the matn: it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay Fajr until isfar (daylight). He explains that although the valid time begins at true dawn, one should wait so that more people can join the congregation, increasing reward. He supports this with the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij where the Prophet explicitly said to perform Fajr at isfar due to greater reward. The author then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i and others, who hold that praying at the earliest time is always better, and for Fajr they prefer gloom (ghalas) based on the hadith of 'Aisha describing women leaving the mosque unrecognizable due to darkness. The author resolves the apparent contradiction by noting context: if people habitually attend early, like in Madinah or in Ramadan, then gloom is preferable; otherwise, isfar is better to ensure a larger congregation. Thus, the Hanafi position is flexible based on local practice, though the default recommendation is isfar.

Key Terms
الاسفار (al-isfar): Daylight; the time when the light of dawn is clearly visible and the darkness has dissipated.
الغلس (al-ghalas): The gloom or darkness before dawn; the earliest part of the Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this lesson, when is it recommended to pray Fajr at ghalas (in darkness)?
A) Always, because it is the earliest time.
B) When the congregation is small and needs to be increased.
C) When the people habitually come to the mosque early, like in Madinah.
D) Never, because the hadith command is to pray at isfar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends isfar for Fajr to maximize congregation, but allows ghalas if people already attend early, reconciling both hadith through contextual analysis.

Ibrad for Zuhr in Summer: Proof and Practice
Clarifies the preferred time for Zuhr in hot weather.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ibrad for Zuhr in summer and identify the primary hadith proof that establishes it.

Core Idea
Ibrad for Zuhr in summer is a confirmed sunnah, derived from the Prophet's command to delay when heat is severe.

The timing of Zuhr prayer varies with seasons. This lesson focuses on the Hanafi recommendation to delay Zuhr in hot weather, known as ibrad. We will examine the hadith evidence and understand why this is considered mustahabb rather than obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that the Hanafi school recommends delaying Zuhr in summer (ibrad) and hastening it in winter (ta'jil). The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling is based on explicit hadith, not merely scholarly opinion.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar where the Prophet said: 'When the heat is severe, cool the prayer, for severe heat is from the blast of Hell.' This is the main proof.
References: Bukhari no.533; Tirmidhi no.157.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand that the imperative 'abridu' indicates recommendation, not obligation, because it is linked to an excusing condition (severe heat). In Hanafi usul, commands with conditional excuses are for recommendation.
The command is not absolute; it is conditioned on heat, showing flexibility.
4
Note supporting proofs
Two additional hadiths from Anas ibn Malik show the Prophet's practice: he hastened Zuhr in cold and delayed it in heat, including for Friday prayer. These confirm the ruling.
The third hadith explicitly mentions Friday, but the ruling is extended to Zuhr by analogy.

Source Text

[۱۴۲] (۹) والابراد بالظهر في الصيف وتقديمها في الشتاء.

مستحب ہے گرمی میں ظہر کو ٹھنڈا کر کے پڑھنا اور سردی میں اس کو مقدم کرنا۔

(1) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ... حدثاه عن رسول الله انه قال اذا اشتد الحر فابردوا بالصلوه فان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم (د) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الا براد بالظهر في شدة الحرص ۶ نمبر ۳۳ ٫۵ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی تا خیر الظهر في شدة الحرص ۴۰، نمبر ۱۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گرمی ہو تو ظہر کی نماز مؤخر کر کے پڑھنا مستحب ہے (۲) اور حدیث میں ہے انس بن مالک ان رسول الله خرج حين زاغت الشمس فصلى الظهر (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقت الظهر عن الزوال ص ۷ے سے نمبر ۵۴۰) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سردی ہو تو نماز جلدی پڑھی جائے۔ ایک دوسری حدیث میں ہے سمعت انس بن مالک يقول كان النبى اذا اشتد البرد بكر بالصلوة وذا اشتد الحر ابرد بالصلوة يعنى الجمعة (الف) ( بخاری شریف باب اذا اشتد الحر يوم الجمعۃ ص ۱۲۴ کتاب الجمعہ نمبر ۹۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سردی میں ظہر کی نماز جلدی پڑھے اور گرمی میں دیر کر کے پڑھے۔
[142] (9) And to cool the noon prayer in summer and hasten it in winter. It is recommended in summer to delay Zuhr until it is cooler, and in winter to hasten it. (1) There is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When the heat is severe, cool the prayer, for severe heat is from the blast of Hell.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Ibrad bil-Zuhr fi Shiddat al-Harr, p.6 no.533; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Ta'khir al-Zuhr fi Shiddat al-Harr, p.40 no.157) This hadith indicates that when it is hot, it is recommended to delay the Zuhr prayer. (2) And there is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah went out when the sun declined and prayed Zuhr. (Bukhari, Bab Waqt al-Zuhr 'an al-Zawal, from p.7 no.540) This indicates that in cold weather, the prayer should be performed early. Another hadith: I heard Anas ibn Malik say: 'When the cold was severe, the Prophet hastened the prayer, and when the heat was severe, he cooled the prayer – meaning the Friday prayer.' (Bukhari, Bab Idha ishtadda al-Harr yawm al-Jumu'ah, p.124 no.906) This hadith indicates that in winter, Zuhr should be prayed early, and in summer, late.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for Zuhr prayer timing. The author states that it is mustahabb to delay Zuhr in summer (ibrad) and to hasten it in winter. He provides three hadith proofs: First, the famous hadith commanding ibrad when heat is intense, attributing it to the heat of Hell. Second, the practice of the Prophet leaving for Zuhr at zawal (declination) in cold weather. Third, a hadith about the Prophet's practice in extreme cold and heat. The commentary also notes that the second hadith about ibrad for Friday applies similarly to Zuhr. The underlying reason is physical comfort and avoiding harm. This is a ruling with proof, and the Hanafi school follows these hadith directly.

Key Terms
الابراد (al-ibrad): To cool or delay a prayer until it is cooler; used for Zuhr in summer.
التعجيل (ta'jil): To hasten a prayer; recommended for Zuhr in winter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ibrad for Zuhr in summer is a sunnah muakkadah established by explicit hadith, reflecting the Prophet's care for ease in worship.

Recommended Delay of Asr Before Yellowness
Explains the recommended time for Asr before yellowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Asr prayer and identify the prophetic practice (fi'l) as its evidence.

Core Idea
Delay Asr while the sun is white, not yellow.

This lesson explains the recommended time for Asr prayer in the Hanafi school. The author advises delaying Asr as long as the sun has not turned yellow, citing the Prophet's consistent practice. This allows time for supererogatory prayers (nawafil) before Asr, which are prohibited after it. You will learn the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying Asr prayer. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. Note the condition: delay only while the sun remains white (before yellowness).
Mustahabb is a non-obligatory recommended action.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: from Abu Dawud and Darqutni, describing the Prophet's practice of delaying Asr while the sun was white.
The hadith are ahad (solitary), so the proof is zanni al-thubut (speculative in transmission).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action (fi'l) indicates recommendation. The phrase 'while the sun remained white' sets the time limit before yellowness.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's habitual actions (fi'l) indicate mandub (recommendation) unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is consider it permissible (ja'iz) to delay Asr until yellowness, though they dislike it after. They do not consider early delay as mustahabb.
The difference stems from interpreting the Prophet's practice: Hanafis see it as a recommended sunnah, Shafi'is as merely permissible.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) based on the authentic practice and the wisdom of allowing supererogatory prayers before Asr.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah upholds this view, though no explicit tarjih is given in this passage.

From these two hadith it is understood that it is recommended to delay Asr prayer until before the sun turns yellow, so that one can pray supererogatory prayers (nawafil) before Asr, because after Asr one cannot pray nawafil.

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended time for Asr prayer. The author states that it is mustahabb to delay Asr as long as the sun remains white and has not turned yellow. He provides two hadith: one shows the Prophet's practice of delaying Asr while the sun was white, and another confirms the same. The reason given is to allow time for supererogatory prayers before Asr, as voluntary prayers are prohibited after Asr until sunset. The Hanafi school considers this delay recommended, not mandatory, and it is based on the explicit practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
تغير الشمس (taghayyur al-shams): The sun turning yellow; after this time, it is makruh to delay Asr.

It is recommended (mustahabb) to delay Asr prayer until just before the sun turns yellow, based on the Prophet's practice, to allow time for supererogatory prayers.

The Recommendation of Hastening Maghrib
States the preferred time for Maghrib immediately after sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening Maghrib and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Pray Maghrib immediately after sunset—this is a confirmed sunnah.

Maghrib has the shortest time window of all prayers. The Prophet ﷺ emphasized praying it promptly. In this lesson, we examine the textual evidence and the Hanafi position that hastening Maghrib is highly recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification. Here, the act is performing Maghrib prayer at the earliest time, and the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended).
2
Examine the first proof
Recall the hadith of Jibril (peace be upon him) who led the Prophet in prayer on two consecutive days, praying Maghrib at the same time both days. This shows there is only one preferred time for Maghrib – its beginning.
This is a well-known hadith in the books of timings.
3
Analyze the second proof
Read the hadith narrated by Abu Ayyub al-Ansari: the Prophet said the ummah will remain in goodness as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars become intertwined. The conditional warning implies that delaying is not good, so hastening is better.
Arabic phrase: 'la tazalu ummati bikhayr ... ma lam yu'akhkhiru al-maghrib ila an tashtabik al-nujum'.
4
Determine the type of obligation
The evidence is from ahad hadith, which yields zanni thubut. Therefore the ruling is not fard but sunnah muakkadah. However, the emphasis is strong.
The Hanafis differentiate between fard (certain) and wajib/mustahabb (less certain).
5
Practical application
The mufta bihi position is to pray Maghrib as soon as the adhan is given after sunset. Delaying without excuse is makruh tanzihi.
Common practice in Hanafi mosques is to pray within a few minutes of sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(2) There is a hadith: Abu Ayyub stood up and said: Did you not hear the Messenger of Allah say: 'My ummah will continue to be in goodness – or he said: upon the fitrah – as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Waqt al-Maghrib, p.66 no.418) From this hadith it is understood that hastening Maghrib is a good thing.

Commentary
This passage addresses the timing of Maghrib. The author states that it is mustahabb to hasten Maghrib, meaning to pray it immediately after sunset at its earliest time. He gives two proofs: first, the well-known hadith of Jibril where he prayed Maghrib at the same time on both the first and second days (i.e., at the very beginning of its time), indicating that there is only one preferred time for Maghrib. Second, the hadith of Abu Ayyub warns against delaying Maghrib until stars appear, implying that early prayer is better. The Hanafi school strongly emphasizes not delaying Maghrib.

Key Terms
تشتبك النجوم (tashtabik al-nujum): The stars become intertwined or thick in the sky – i.e., after twilight and darkness has set in.

Key Takeaway
Hastening Maghrib is a confirmed sunnah; delaying it until stars intertwine diminishes the reward.

Recommendation of Delaying Isha Until One-Third of the Night
Clarifies the preferred time for Isha prayer before midnight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Isha, explain the proof from the hadith, and apply the ruling considering hardship.

Core Idea
Delaying Isha to one-third of the night is recommended, not obligatory, because the Prophet refrained from commanding it due to hardship.

This lesson explains the preferred time for Isha prayer. The Hanafi school holds that delaying it until one-third of the night is highly recommended (mustahabb), but not mandatory. The evidence is a powerful hadith where the Prophet desired to command delay but did not out of mercy. Understanding this ruling helps you balance following the sunnah with practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying Isha prayer from its earliest time. The Hanafi ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended), falling under sunnah muakkadah. This means it is strongly encouraged but not obligatory.
The author explicitly uses 'مستحب' (mustahabb).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah: the Prophet said he would command delay if not for hardship. This hadith is found in Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
The text quotes the Arabic: لو لا ان اشق على امتى لامرتهم ان يؤخروا العشاء الى ثلث الليل او نصفه.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'law la' (لولا) indicates a conditional that prevents a command due to a hindrance. The Prophet's desire to command shows the action is beloved, but the omission due to hardship proves it is not obligatory. Thus, it is a recommended act.
This is a classic example of extracting a ruling from the absence of an obligation.
4
Note cross-madhhab agreement
Both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree that delaying Isha is recommended. However, Hanafis emphasize delaying to one-third, while some Shafi'is prefer the earlier part of the night.
The practical difference is minimal; both schools consider the prayer valid if done early.
5
Apply the ruling with consideration of hardship
If delaying causes genuine hardship (e.g., cold, travel, illness), it is permissible to pray Isha at its earliest time. The sunnah is not to cause difficulty; mercy is prioritized.
This follows the principle that necessity overrides the recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۵) (۱۲) عشا کو تہائی رات تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔

حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله له لو لا ان اشق على امتى لامرتهم ان يؤخروا العشاء الى ثلث الليل او نصفه (ه) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تا خیر العشاء الآخرة میں ۴۲ نمبر ۱۶۷ را ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما وقت العشاء الآخرة ص حاشیه : : (الف) آپ نے پوری ہی رات وتر پڑھی۔ شروع رات میں، درمیان میں اور آخر میں ۔ آخری آپ کی و ترجب انتقال کیا سحری کے وقت تھی (ب) آپ فرمایا کرتے تھے فجر کو اسفار کر کے پڑھو اس میں اجر و ثواب زیادہ ہے (ج) حضرت عائشہ نے خبر دی کہ مومن عورتیں حضور کے ساتھ فجر کی نماز میں حاضر ہوتیں اپنی چادروں میں لپٹ کر۔ پھر اپنے گھروں کو جاتیں جس وقت نماز پوری کر لیتیں تو وہ اندھیرے کی وجہ سے پہچانی نہیں جاتیں (د) آپ نے فرمایا اگر گرمی زیادہ ہو تو نماز ٹھنڈی کر کے پڑھو۔ اس لئے کہ سخت گرمی جہنم کی لپیٹ میں سے ہے (ہ) آپ نکلے سورج ڈھل گیا اور ظہر کی نماز پڑھی۔
(145) (12) It is recommended to delay Isha prayer up to one-third of the night. In a hadith from Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Were it not for hardship upon my ummah, I would command them to delay Isha until one-third or half of the night.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Ta'khir al-Isha al-Akhira, no.167; Abu Dawud, Bab ma Waqt al-Isha al-Akhira) [Footnote: He prayed Witr the entire night: beginning, middle, and end. His last Witr was at the time of suhur.]
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing of Isha prayer. The author states that it is mustahabb to delay Isha up to one-third of the night (or half, as in the hadith). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet expressed a desire to command delay but refrained due to hardship. This indicates that delay is better but not obligatory. The Hanafi school takes this as a recommendation to delay Isha, but if it causes hardship, it is permissible to pray earlier at the beginning of its time. The footnote mentions that the Prophet prayed Witr at various times of the night, but that is a separate point.

Key Terms
تأخير العشاء (ta'khir al-isha): Delaying the Isha prayer from its earliest time until up to one-third or half of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet not command delaying Isha?
A) Because it is not recommended
B) Because it would cause hardship
C) Because the time was limited
D) Because the companions preferred early prayer

Key Takeaway
Delaying Isha to one-third of the night is a recommended sunnah (mustahabb), not an obligation, and hardship justifies praying earlier.

Ruling on Delaying 'Asr Prayer until Sun Yellows
States ruling and proof for delaying 'Asr until sun yellows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying 'Asr prayer and explain the proof from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
Delaying 'Asr until yellowness is recommended to allow supererogatory prayers before the prohibited time.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding the preferred time for 'Asr prayer. The Hanafi school holds that it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay 'Asr until the sun shows yellowness, based on the Prophet's own practice. The wisdom behind this is to make room for sunnah and nafl prayers before 'Asr, which cannot be performed afterwards. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Clearly state what act is being ruled upon and the level of the ruling (mustahabb/sunnah).
The act is delaying the 'Asr prayer until the sun becomes yellow.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
Identify the two hadiths cited and note that they describe the Prophet's action (fi'l).
Both hadiths show the Prophet delaying 'Asr while the sun was still white.
3
Understand the Indication (Wajh al-Dalalah)
Analyze how the Prophet's action indicates recommendation, not obligation, in Hanafi usul.
The Prophet's continuous practice on a non-obligatory act shows it is sunnah; there is no command to delay.
4
Note the Wisdom (Hikmah)
Explain the reason given: to allow time for supererogatory prayers before 'Asr.
After 'Asr, voluntary prayers are prohibited (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school.
5
Compare with Opposing View
Briefly mention that the Shafi'i school considers delaying until yellowness makruh tahrimi.
Shafi'is hold that 'Asr time ends with yellowness, so delaying is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٤٣] (١٠) وتاخير العصر مالم تتغير الشمس.
عصر مؤخر کرے جب تک سورج میں زردی نہ آجائے۔
(1) حدیث میں ہے علی بن شيبان قال قدمنا على رسول الله الا الله الى المدينة فكان يؤخر العصر مادامت الشمس بيضاء بقية (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وقت صلوۃ العصر ص ۶۵ نمبر ۴۰۸) (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے سمعت ابا مسعود الانصارى يقول ... ورأيته يصلى العصر والشمس مرتفعة بيضاء قبل ان تدخلها الصفرة (ج) (دارقطنى، باب ذکر بیان المواقيت و اختلاف الروايات في ذلك ج اول ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۹۷۵) ان دونوں احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آفتاب زرد ہونے سے پہلے تک عصر کی نماز مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔ تا کہ عصر سے پہلے سفن اور نوافل پڑھ سکے۔ کیونکہ عصر کی نماز کے بعد نوافل نہیں پڑھ سکیں گے۔
[143] (10) And delay 'Asr as long as the sun has not changed. Delay 'Asr until the sun becomes yellow. (1) In a hadith, Ali ibn Shayban said: We came to the Messenger of Allah in Madinah, and he used to delay 'Asr as long as the sun remained white. (Abu Dawud, Book of Prayer Times, #408) (2) Another hadith: I heard Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari say: ... I saw him praying 'Asr while the sun was high and white before yellowness entered it. (Darqutni, Book of Mentioning Times and Differences of Narrations, Vol 1, p259 #975) From these two hadiths it is understood that it is mustahabb to delay 'Asr prayer until before the sun becomes yellow. So that one can pray the supererogatory (sunan and nawafil) before 'Asr, because after 'Asr one cannot pray nawafil.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of 'Asr prayer. The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay 'Asr prayer until the sun shows yellowness. The proof comes from two hadiths: the first from Ali ibn Shayban shows the Prophet delaying 'Asr while the sun remained white; the second from Abu Mas'ud confirms the same. The wisdom is to allow time for sunnah and nafl prayers before 'Asr, since after 'Asr these voluntary prayers are prohibited (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; reward for doing, no sin for leaving.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): Emphasized sunnah; the Prophet consistently performed it; leaving it is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To have time to pray sunnah and nafl prayers before 'Asr.
C) Because the Prophet commanded to delay until yellowness.
D) To combine it with Maghrib.

Key Takeaway
Delaying 'Asr until the sun yellows is mustahabb in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice, to allow supererogatory prayers before the prohibited time.

Ruling on Delaying 'Isha Prayer
States ruling and proof for delaying 'Isha until one-third of the night

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying 'Isha prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Delaying 'Isha until one-third of the night is mustahabb, not wajib, due to the Prophet's consideration of hardship.

This lesson explores the preferred time for 'Isha prayer. The Hanafi school considers delaying it until one-third of the night as a sunnah, based on a hadith where the Prophet refrained from making it obligatory due to potential hardship. Understanding this ruling helps balance following the sunnah with practical considerations for the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? (Delaying 'Isha prayer) What is the hukm? (mustahabb/sunnah)
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite? (The hadith from Abu Hurayra)
The hadith is reported by Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the recommendation? The Prophet's conditional statement shows his intent to command, but the hardship exemption indicates it is not obligatory.
The phrase 'if it were not for hardship' indicates the act is recommended, not required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement among schools? (All schools agree on recommendation; minor differences on exact time limit)
The Hanafi position is consistent with other schools on this matter.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position relied upon? (Based on clear hadith and consistent with the principle of avoiding hardship)
The mufta bihi is to delay until one-third, provided no hardship.

The Recommended Timing of Witr Prayer
States ruling on when to pray Witr for those who pray Tahajjud vs. those who don't

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended time for Witr and apply the prophetic conditional to determine when to pray it based on one's confidence in waking up.

Core Idea
Delay Witr to the end of the night for those certain to wake; pray before sleep for those who fear missing.

Witr is a wajib prayer in the Hanafi school, performed after 'Isha until just before Fajr. While the entire window is valid, the Prophet ﷺ taught a nuanced recommendation based on a person's wakefulness habits. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its underlying proof, helping you tailor your practice to your own consistency in Tahajjud.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the two categories of people
The passage distinguishes between (a) one who is accustomed to night prayer (Tahajjud) and confident in waking, and (b) one who fears he may not wake up.
2
2. Extract the ruling for each category
For those confident: delaying Witr to the last part of the night is mustahabb (recommended). For those uncertain: praying Witr before sleeping is recommended to avoid missing it entirely.
3
3. Locate the dalil and its wording
The hadith from Jabir (Muslim #755) provides the explicit basis. The Prophet said: 'Whoever fears he will not get up at the end of the night should pray Witr at its beginning, and whoever hopes to wake up at the end should pray Witr at the end...'
4
4. Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The conditional 'man khāfa' and 'man ṭamiʻa' set a principle: the ruling depends on one's expectation. The phrase 'that is better' indicates preference for delay when possible.
5
5. Formulate the Hanafi position
Combining the hadith and Hanafi usul, the mufta bihi is: delaying Witr is superior for those confident of waking, but early prayer is acceptable and even recommended for those who fear oversleeping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٤٦] (١٣) ويستحب في الوتر لمن يالف صلوة الليل ان يؤخر الوتر الى آخر الليل وان لم يثق بالانتباه اوتر قبل النوم.
وتر میں مستحب اس شخص کے لئے جس کو تہجد پڑھنے کا شوق ہو یہ ہے کہ مؤخر کرے رات کے اخیر حصہ تک ، اور اگر اعتماد نہ ہو جاگنے پر تو وتر پڑھے سونے سے پہلے۔

صلى الله حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال قال رسول الله الله من خاف ان لا يقوم من آخر الليل فليوتر اوله ومن طمع ان يقوم آخره فليوتر آخر الليل فان صلوة آخر الليل مشهودة و ذلك افضل (الف) (مسلم شریف، بابمن خاف ان لا يقوم من آخر الليل فليوتر اوله ، ص ۲۵۸، نمبر ۷۵۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وتر اخیر میں پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن اگر سو جانے کا خطرہ ہو تو سونے سے پہلے پڑھ لینا چاہئے۔
حق بالانتباہ : جاگنے پر اعتماد ہو۔
[146] (13) And it is mustahabb in Witr for the one who is accustomed to night prayer to delay Witr until the end of the night, and if he does not trust that he will wake up, he should pray Witr before sleeping. In Witr, it is mustahabb for the one who has enthusiasm for Tahajjud to delay until the last part of the night. And if he does not have confidence in waking up, he should pray Witr before sleeping. In a hadith: Jabir said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever fears that he will not wake up at the end of the night should pray Witr at its beginning, and whoever hopes to wake up at the end should pray Witr at the end, for the prayer at the end of the night is witnessed and that is better.' (Muslim, Book of Whoever Fears Not Waking at End of Night, #755). From this hadith it is understood that Witr should be prayed at the end, but if there is fear of sleeping through, one should pray before sleeping. Haqq bil-intibah: confidence in waking up.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for the recommended time of Witr prayer, differentiated by the person's habit. For one who regularly prays Tahajjud (night prayer), the sunnah is to delay Witr to the last part of the night, so that Witr becomes the seal of the night prayer. For one who fears he may not wake up, it is better to pray Witr before sleeping. The proof is the hadith from Jabir where the Prophet gives the option based on confidence. The phrase 'prayer at the end of the night is witnessed' refers to angels witnessing it, making it more virtuous. In the Hanafi school, Witr is wajib, and its time is after 'Isha until dawn; this ruling concerns the preferred time within that window.

Key Terms
وط (watr): The Witr prayer; an odd-numbered prayer after 'Isha, wajib in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) At the end of the night, after Tahajjud.
C) In the middle of the night.
D) Immediately after 'Isha.

Key Takeaway
Delay Witr to the end of the night if you are confident of waking; otherwise, pray before sleeping to safeguard the wajib.
