6 min
Recommended Timing of Witr: Delay if Confident of Waking
Explains the recommended timing of Witr for those who pray Tahajjud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended timing of Witr according to the Hanafi school and apply the criterion of confidence in waking to determine the appropriate time.

Core Idea
Delay Witr to the end of the night if confident of waking; otherwise pray before sleeping.

Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, but its timing is not fixed. The Prophet ﷺ gave a clear guideline based on one's confidence in waking for Tahajjud. This lesson unpacks that guideline and its application, helping you align your practice with the sunnah while avoiding unnecessary risk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act here is delaying Witr. The ruling category is 'mustahab' (recommended), not wajib. Understand that the obligation (wajib) is to pray Witr itself; its timing is flexible.
Don't confuse the ruling of the prayer (wajib) with the ruling of its timing (mustahab).
2
Recognize the two scenarios
The hadith presents two cases: (1) one who fears not waking at the end, and (2) one who hopes to wake. Identify which scenario applies to you.
The key criterion is 'confidence in waking' (al-intibah).
3
Apply the criterion to your situation
If you are confident you will wake up for Tahajjud, delay Witr to the last part of the night. If not confident or unsure, pray Witr before sleeping.
Confidence here means a reasonable expectation based on habit or schedule.
4
Understand the evidence
The hadith from Jabir (ra) explicitly gives the two options and states that the end-of-night prayer is 'witnessed' and better. This is the proof for the recommendation.
The imperative 'فليوتر' indicates recommendation, not obligation.
5
Note the wisdom
Delaying Witr to the end allows it to be the last prayer before Fajr, which is virtuous. But the priority is to ensure the prayer is performed, so the early option is for those uncertain.
This flexibility shows the mercy of the Shariah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب في الوتر لمن يالف صلوة الليل ان يؤخر الوتر الى آخر الليل وان لم يثق بالانتباه اوتر قبل النوم . ( اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کی نماز کو تہائی رات تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔ ) ( وتر میں مستحب اس شخص کے لئے جس کو تہجد پڑھنے کا شوق ہو یہ ہے کہ مؤخر کرے رات کے اخیر حصہ تک ، اور اگر اعتماد نہ ہو جاگنے پر تو وتر پڑھے سونے سے پہلے۔ جس کو تہجد پڑھنے کا شوق اور عادت ہو وہ وتر رات کے اخیر حصہ میں پڑھے۔ اور جسکو جاگنے پر اعتماد نہ ہو تو اس کو سونے سے پہلے وتر پڑھ لینا چاہئے۔ صلى الله حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال قال رسول الله الله من خاف ان لا يقوم من آخر الليل فليوتر اوله ومن طمع ان يقوم آخره فليوتر آخر الليل فان صلوة آخر الليل مشهودة و ذلك افضل (الف) (مسلم شریف، بابمن خاف ان لا يقوم من آخر الليل فليوتر اوله ، ص ۲۵۸، نمبر ۷۵۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وتر اخیر میں پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن اگر سو جانے کا خطرہ ہو تو سونے سے پہلے پڑھ لینا چاہئے۔ حق بالانتباہ : جاگنے پر اعتماد ہو )
It is recommended in Witr for one who is accustomed to night prayer to delay Witr to the last part of the night, and if he does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleeping. (From this it is known that it is recommended to delay Isha prayer until one third of the night.) (In Witr, it is recommended for the person who has enthusiasm for Tahajjud to delay until the last part of the night, and if he does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleeping. The one who has enthusiasm and habit for Tahajjud should pray Witr in the last part of the night. And the one who does not trust himself to wake up should pray Witr before sleeping. In the hadith from Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever fears that he will not get up at the end of the night, let him pray Witr at its beginning, and whoever hopes to get up at the end, let him pray Witr at the end, for the prayer at the end of the night is witnessed and that is better.' (Muslim, chapter: Whoever fears that he will not get up at the end of the night, let him pray Witr at its beginning, p. 258, no. 755) From this hadith it is known that Witr should be prayed at the end, but if there is a fear of sleeping, it should be prayed before sleeping. Haqq bi al-intibah: Confidence in waking up.)
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the timing of the Witr prayer. The author states a general recommendation: for a person who is accustomed to offering night prayer (Tahajjud), it is mustahab (recommended) to delay the Witr prayer until the last part of the night. However, if one does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleeping. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this also implies it is recommended to delay the Isha prayer until one-third of the night. The proof is a hadith from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet ﷺ gives the choice based on one's confidence in waking up, indicating that the end-of-night prayer is witnessed by angels and is superior. The Arabic word 'حق بالانتباہ' defines 'al-intibah' as confidence in waking. The Hanafi school follows this ruling: Witr itself is wajib, but its timing is flexible based on certainty of waking.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer that concludes the night prayer; wajib in the Hanafi school.
يستحب (yustahabbu): It is recommended; a ruling category between wajib and mubah.
الانتباه (al-intibah): Waking up from sleep; here it refers to confidence in waking up for Tahajjud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should a person who is confident of waking up for Tahajjud pray Witr?
A) Immediately after Isha prayer
B) At the end of the night
C) At midnight
D) Before sleeping regardless

Key Takeaway
The timing of Witr is flexible and based on one's confidence in waking for Tahajjud; the best is to delay for those confident, otherwise pray before sleeping.

The Ruling of Adhan and the Issue of Tarji'
States sunnah status of Adhan and denies tarji'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah status of Adhan for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, and explain why the Hanafi school does not recognize tarji' in the Adhan.

Core Idea
Adhan is a stressed sunnah for five prayers and Jumu'ah; tarji' is a Shafi'i addition not supported by the original practice.

This passage marks the beginning of the chapter on Adhan, establishing its legal status as sunnah muakkadah for the daily and Friday prayers, and then delves into the disputed issue of tarji' (repetition of the two shahadahs in a low then loud voice). The Hanafi school firmly rejects tarji' based on the practice of Abdullah bin Zaid and the Prophet's own method, while the Shafi'i school includes it. Understanding both the ruling and the dispute is essential for proper practice and for respecting valid scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
First, note that Adhan is sunnah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah only. Second, note that there is no tarji' in the Adhan according to the Hanafi school.
The passage clearly separates these two points.
2
State the Hanafi position on tarji'
The Hanafi school holds that tarji' is not part of the Adhan; the Adhan should be recited in pairs (each phrase twice) without any change in volume.
Tarji' means repeating the shahadahs softly then loudly.
3
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam Shafi'i holds that tarji' is part of the Adhan, relying on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah where the Prophet taught him the Adhan with repetition.
Opponent: Shafi'i school. Their proof: a hadith in Sahih Muslim.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the repetition in Abu Mahdhurah's case was specifically to raise his voice, not to establish a general sunnah. The established practice from the Prophet and Companions is without tarji'.
Hanafi evidence: hadith of Abdullah bin Zaid that the Prophet's Adhan was in pairs without volume change.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is in how the Adhan is performed: Hanafi mu'adhdhin says each phrase twice at the same volume; Shafi'i says the shahadahs twice softly then twice loudly.
This difference is noticeable in audio but both are valid within their schools.

Chapter of Adhan. The Adhan is Sunnah for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, not for others. And there is no tarji' in the Adhan. (Necessary note: Adhan means announcement; in Adhan, the prayer is announced, so it is called Adhan. Its proof is from the verse: 'O you who have believed, when [the adhan] is called for the prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, then proceed to the remembrance of Allah' (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9). (Adhan is Sunnah for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, not for others. The meaning of Adhan not being Sunnah besides the five prayers and Jumu'ah is that it is not Sunnah to give Adhan for (1) Witr, (2) the two Eids, (3) Janazah, (4) Khusuf (eclipse), (5) Istisqa' (rain prayer), (6) Tarawih, (7) the supererogatory sunan. The proof that Adhan is Sunnah is the hadith that Ibn Umar used to say: 'When the Muslims came to Madinah, they would gather and wait for the prayer, and it was not called for them. One day they talked about that. Some said: Take a bell like the bell of the Christians. Some said: Rather a trumpet like the horn of the Jews. Then Umar said: Will you not send a man to call for the prayer? Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: O Bilal, stand and call for the prayer.' (Bukhari, chapter: Beginning of Adhan, p. 85, no. 604; Muslim, chapter: Beginning of Adhan, p. 64, no. 37) From this hadith it is known that giving Adhan for prayer is Sunnah. (There is no tarji' in the Adhan. Explanation of tarji': It is to say 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah' two times softly, then repeat these two phrases two times loudly. So it is the repetition of these two phrases, therefore it is called tarji'. According to the Hanafis, there is no tarji' in the Adhan. One: Abdullah bin Zaid, who saw the angel giving Adhan in his dream and taught the words of Adhan to Bilal, did not have tarji'. From Abdullah bin Zaid: 'The Adhan of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was in pairs in the Adhan and the Iqamah.' (Tirmidhi, chapter: What has come about the Iqamah being in pairs, p. 48, no. 194; Abu Dawud, chapter: How is the Adhan, p. 78, no. 499) The Prophet ﷺ made Abu Mahdhurah repeat the two shahadahs loudly to raise his voice, so he thought that tarji' was original. However, making him repeat the two shahadahs was to raise his voice, not as a principle. According to Imam Shafi'i, there is tarji' in the Adhan. His proof is the long hadith of Abu Mahdhurah. This hadith is in Muslim.)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the chapter on Adhan in the sharh. It first defines Adhan linguistically and then provides the ruling: Adhan is Sunnah (recommended) for the five daily prayers and the Friday prayer only, not for other prayers like Witr, Eid, Janazah, eclipse, rain prayer, Tarawih, or other supererogatory prayers. The proof is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) which commands hastening to the remembrance of Allah when the call is made, and the hadith about the beginning of Adhan in Madinah where the Prophet instructed Bilal to call the prayer. The second part addresses the issue of tarji' (repetition of the two shahadahs in a low then loud voice). The Hanafi school holds that there is no tarji' in the Adhan. The evidence is the hadith of Abdullah bin Zaid that the Prophet's Adhan was in pairs (each phrase twice without differentiating volume). The Shafi'i school holds that tarji' is part of the Adnan, relying on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah. The Hanafi response is that Abu Mahdhurah's repetition was for the purpose of raising his voice, not as a permanent sunnah. The text concludes the Hanafi position as the correct one.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, announcing the start of the prayer time.
الترجيع (at-tarji'): Repetition of the two shahadahs (Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah and Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah) in a low voice then a loud voice.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice; an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Jumu'ah prayer
D) Janazah prayer

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a sunnah muakkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah only, and the Hanafi school does not recognize tarji' as part of the Adhan.

Adhan is Sunnah for Five Prayers and Jumu'ah
Ruling that adhan is sunnah only for five daily prayers and Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that establishes it as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah only.

This passage begins the section on adhan by clearly stating its legal status: it is a recommended practice (sunnah) for the five obligatory prayers and the Friday prayer. The author then clarifies that adhan is not prescribed for any other prayers, such as Witr, Eid, or funeral prayer. The proof is drawn from both the Quranic verse that mentions 'the call' on Friday and the hadith in which the Prophet instructed Bilal to call the adhan.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (adhan) and its legal category (sunnah mu'akkadah) as given in the matn.
The Arabic phrase 'سنة' indicates a recommended practice, not an obligation.
2
Define the scope
List the specific prayers for which adhan is sunnah (the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah) and those for which it is not (Witr, Eids, Janazah, etc.).
The Urdu commentary explicitly lists the excluded prayers.
3
Locate the Quranic evidence
Identify the verse (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) that mentions 'when the call is made' as a proof for the legitimacy of adhan.
The verse is cited as a dalil that adhan was a known practice.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
Review the hadith of Ibn Umar describing how the Prophet instructed Bilal to call the adhan, which establishes the practice as a sunnah.
The imperative 'qum fanadi' is understood in Hanafi usul to indicate recommendation, not obligation, due to other evidence.

Commentary
This passage begins the section on adhan in the Book of Prayer. The author first states the ruling: adhan is sunnah (recommended) for the five daily prayers and for Jumu'ah, but not for any other prayers. The Urdu commentary explains that 'other than them' includes Witr, the two Eids, funeral prayer, eclipse prayer, rain prayer, Tarawih, and additional sunnah prayers. The proof is from the Quranic verse in Surah al-Jumu'ah (62:9) which commands hastening to the remembrance of Allah when the call is made on Friday, indicating the legitimacy of adhan. Additionally, a hadith from Ibn Umar describes the consultation of the Companions about how to announce prayer, and eventually the Prophet instructed Bilal to call the adhan. This hadith is a primary proof that adhan is a sunnah practice established by the Prophet.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases announcing the times of obligatory prayers, sunnah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omission is not sinful but is disliked.

No Tarji' in Adhan (Hanafi View)
Ruling that tarji' is not part of adhan, with evidence from Abdullah ibn Zaid and rebuttal of Abu Mahdhurah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarji' in adhan, identify the evidence from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-evidence from Abu Mahdhurah.

Core Idea
Tarji' in adhan is rejected by Hanafis because the Prophet's adhan was shifa' shifa' (in pairs) without soft-loud repetition.

This passage tackles an important difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the adhan. The specific point is whether the shahadahs should be repeated softly then loudly (tarji') or just twice in a normal voice. The Hanafi position is clear: there is no tarji'. Let's examine the evidence and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that tarji' is not part of adhan. Note that the adhan is recited in pairs (shifa' shifa') without soft-loud repetition.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tarji' is part of adhan based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, where the Prophet taught him to repeat the shahadahs twice softly then twice loudly.
3
Follow the Hanafi refutation
Analyze how Hanafis explain the Abu Mahdhurah narration: the repetition was for voice training, not a sunna. Also, the Darqutni version lacks tarji'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: in a Hanafi adhan, the shahadahs are recited twice in a normal voice; in a Shafi'i adhan, they are recited twice softly and twice loudly.
5
Conclude with tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school because the evidence from the majority of practices (Bilal, Abdullah ibn Zaid) is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۸) (۲) ولا ترجيع في الاذان. تشر ترجمیع کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اشهد ان لا اله الا الله اور اشهد ان محمدا رسول اللہ کو دو دو مرتبہ آہستہ آہستہ کہے پھر ان دونوں کلمات کو دو دو مرتبہ زور زور سے کہے۔ تو ان دونوں کلمات کو دوبارہ لوٹانا ہے اس لئے اس کو تر جمیع کہتے ہیں۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک اذان میں ترجیع نہیں ہے (۱) عبداللہ بن زید جس نے فرشتے کو خواب میں اذان دیتے ہوئے دیکھا اور حجرت بلال کو اذان کے کلمات کی تلقین کی اس میں ترجیع نہیں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن زيد قال كان اذان رسول الله الله شفعا شفعا في الاذان والاقامة (ج) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ان الاقامه شنی شنی ص ۴۸ نمبر ۱۹۴ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب کیف الاذان ص ۷۸ نمبر ۴۹۹) حضرت ابومحذورہ کو آپ نے آواز بلند کروانے کے لئے دوبارہ شہادتین پڑھوایا تو انہوں نے سمجھا کہ ترجیع اصل ہے۔ حالانکہ دو بور شہادتین پڑھوانا آواز بلند کروانے کے لئے تھا نا امام شافعی کے نزدیک اذان میں ترجیع ہے۔ ان کی دلیل حضرت ابو محذورہ کی لمبی حدیث ہے۔ یہ حدیث مسلم شریف، باب صفته الاذان ص ۶۵ نمبر ۳۷۹ / ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الترجيع فی الاذان ص ۴۸ نمبر ۱۹۲ میں تفصیل سے ہے۔ ابو محذورة کی حدیث جو دار قطنی میں ہے اس میں ترجمع نہیں ہے۔ (دار قطنی ، باب فی ذکر اذان ابی محذورة واختلاف الروایات فیر ص ۲۴۱ نمبر ۸۹۲) اس حدیث میں ترجیع کے کلمات نہیں ہیں۔
[148] (2) And there is no tarji' in the adhan. Explanation: The meaning of tarji' is that one says 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah' twice softly, then says these two phrases twice loudly. This repeating of the two phrases is called tarji'. According to the Hanafis, there is no tarji' in adhan. (1) Abdullah ibn Zaid, who saw the angel giving adhan in a dream and taught the phrases to Bilal, had no tarji' in it. Abdullah ibn Zaid said: The adhan of the Messenger of Allah was in pairs, pairs, in the adhan and iqamah. (Tirmidhi, chapter on iqamah being in pairs; Abu Dawud, chapter on how the adhan is said). The Prophet made Abu Mahdhurah repeat the two shahadahs to raise his voice, so he thought that tarji' was the original practice. However, making him repeat the two shahadahs was to raise his voice, not as an essential part. According to Imam Shafi'i, there is tarji' in adhan. His proof is the lengthy hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, which is detailed in Muslim, chapter on the description of adhan; Tirmidhi, chapter on tarji' in adhan. The hadith of Abu Mahdhurah in Darqutni does not contain tarji' (Darqutni, chapter on the adhan of Abu Mahdhurah and the differences of narrations, p.241 no.892). That hadith does not include the words of tarji'.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of tarji' in adhan. The author defines tarji' as repeating the two shahadahs (testimonies) softly first, then loudly. The Hanafi ruling is that tarji' is not part of adhan. Evidence comes from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid, who learned the adhan from an angel; in that adhan, phrases were said twice in succession without soft-loud repetition. The Prophet's statement that 'adhan is shifa' shifa' (in pairs) supports this. The Shafi'i position, based on Abu Mahdhurah's practice, is that tarji' is part of adhan. The Hanafi response explains that the Prophet only asked Abu Mahdhurah to repeat the shahadahs to train his voice, not as a permanent sunna. Moreover, the version in Darqutni lacks tarji'. Thus, the Hanafi view is that tarji' is not legislated.

Key Terms
ترجيع (tarji'): The practice of reciting the two shahadahs softly first, then repeating them loudly in adhan.
شفعا شفعا (shifa' shifa'): In pairs; each phrase of the adhan is said twice consecutively.
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the adhan of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was:
A) With tarji'
B) Without tarji'
C) Sometimes with tarji'
D) Only for Fajr

Key Takeaway
Tarji' is not part of adhan in the Hanafi school because the original adhan taught by the angel and practiced by Bilal and Abdullah ibn Zaid was without repetition of shahadahs in different pitches.

Addition in Fajr Adhan: الصلاة خير من النوم
Ruling to add 'prayer is better than sleep' twice in Fajr adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the addition of 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The phrase 'prayer is better than sleep' is a sunnah addition exclusive to the Fajr adhan, supported by direct prophetic instruction.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan. While the standard adhan is uniform across prayers, the Fajr adhan has a unique addition to encourage early rising for prayer. The source text provides the rule and its proof from two hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? (adding a phrase in the Fajr adhan). What is the legal ruling? (sunnah mu'akkadah).
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is a recommended sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Which hadiths are cited? The hadith of Bilal stating that alteration is only allowed in Fajr, and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah where the Prophet explicitly instructed to insert the phrase.
Both hadiths are from reliable sources (Tirmidhi, Darqutni).
3
Understand the specification
Why only Fajr? The Prophet's instruction to Bilal and the direct command to Abu Mahdhurah indicate that this phrase is exclusive to Fajr prayer.
This addition distinguishes Fajr adhan from all other prayers.
4
Note the number of times
How many times should it be said? The text states 'مرتين' (twice).
The Hanafi school emphasizes saying it twice.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab status
This practice is agreed upon by most schools, though there may be differences in wording or number of repetitions.
It is a point of ikhtilaf but widely accepted.

Iqamah is Similar to Adhan with Additions
Ruling that iqamah is like adhan but with 'qad qamati al-salah' twice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the iqamah's repetition and identify the key difference with the Shafi'i school based on hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The Hanafi iqamah is recited in pairs like the adhan, supported by multiple hadiths of the Prophet.

This lesson examines the structure of the iqamah and the evidence for its repetition. Understanding the Hanafi view rooted in prophetic practice and the point of disagreement with the Shafi'i school is essential for correct practice and respect for valid scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi iqamah is recited in pairs (muthanna muthanna), each phrase twice, with the addition of 'qad qamati al-salah' after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
The exception mentioned is the addition of 'qad qamati al-salah', which is also said twice.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Review the three hadiths cited: from Ibn Abi Layla, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and Abu Mahdhurah. Note that each indicates the Prophet performed the iqamah in pairs.
These hadiths are from Abu Dawud and are considered authentic by Hanafis.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Connect the hadith wording ('muthanna muthanna' and 'like it except that he said...') to the ruling that each phrase is repeated twice.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Contrast the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i position that iqamah is single (farda) except for 'qad qamati al-salah'. Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The conflict is about the number of repetitions, not the validity of the iqamah.

According to the Hanafis, like the adhan, the iqamah is also in pairs, i.e., two by two, not one by one. Its proof is a hadith that passed in issue number two. Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on iqamah: it is similar to adhan in structure, with the addition of 'qad qamati al-salah' after 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and it is recited in pairs (muthanna muthanna) — meaning each phrase is said twice. The evidence comes from several hadiths: the practice of the Prophet as reported by Ibn Abi Layla and Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and the teaching of Abu Mahdhurah. The Shafi'i position is that iqamah is recited singly (farda farda) — each phrase once — except for 'qad qamati al-salah'. The Hanafi school relies on the hadiths that show the Prophet performed iqamah in pairs. Thus, the practical difference is that Hanafis say each phrase twice, while Shafi'is say them once.

Key Terms
مثنى مثنى (muthanna muthanna): In pairs, i.e., each phrase is recited twice in both adhan and iqamah.
اقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer, just before the prayer begins, consisting of phrases similar to adhan with the addition of 'qad qamati al-salah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi iqamah is recited in pairs (each phrase twice), based on hadith evidence, differing from the Shafi'i single recitation.

Tarassul in Adhan and Hadr in Iqamah: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proof
Ruling on reciting adhan slowly and iqamah quickly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the manner of reciting adhan and iqamah, and explain the evidence from hadith while distinguishing between mustahabb and wajib.

Core Idea
Tarassul in adhan and hadr in iqamah are mustahabb, not wajib, according to the Hanafi school.

This passage from the matn instructs the mu'adhdhin to recite the adhan slowly (tarassul) and the iqamah quickly (hadr). The commentary explains the practical wisdom: the adhan must reach far, while the iqamah is only for those near the mosque. It also clarifies the Hanafi position that this manner is mustahabb (recommended) based on hadith from Anas and Jabir, and that other schools may consider it obligatory. You will learn the ruling, its proof, and the reason why the Hanafis do not consider it wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of reciting adhan with tarassul (slowly with pauses) and iqamah with hadr (quickly). The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), as stated in the text: 'This is mustahabb.'
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: (1) Anas reports that Bilal was commanded to make the adhan in pairs and the iqamah in odd numbers. (2) Jabir reports the Prophet directly told Bilal: 'When you give adhan, recite slowly (tarassul), and when you give iqamah, recite quickly (hadr).'
The hadith are from Sahih Bukhari, Muslim, and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'fahdir' (so make quick) is in the imperative form. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation unless there is a countervailing evidence. Here, the Hanafis consider it recommendation (nadb) due to other evidence and istihsan (juristic preference).
The imperatives are interpreted as guidance for best practice, not legal compulsion.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The majority of imams also consider it mustahabb, but some might view it as wajib. The Hanafi school explicitly says there is no sin if one does the opposite, only a loss of virtue.
The text states: 'Even if one gives the iqamah in odd numbers here, there is no karahah in it; only a difference in afdaliyyah.'
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that tarassul and hadr are mustahabb. This is based on the hadith and the practical wisdom mentioned. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that it is recommended but not obligatory.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah. Cross-madhhab: mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے حکم دیا بلال کو کہ اذان کو شفع کرے اور اقامت کو تر کرے مگر قد قامت الصلوۃ کو
(5) And he should recite slowly in the adhan and quickly in the iqamah. Evidence: many hadith. For example, from Anas: He said, 'Bilal was commanded to make the adhan in pairs and the iqamah in odd numbers, except the iqamah [i.e., except 'qad qamat al-salah' which is said twice]' (a). Due to these hadith, the majority of imams consider it mustahabb to recite the iqamah in odd numbers. The Hanafis say: Even if one gives the iqamah in odd numbers here, there is no karahah in it; only a difference in afdaliyyah. (151) (5) He should do it with pauses in the adhan and quickly in the iqamah. In adhan, the voice is to reach far; therefore, he should utter the words with pauses. In iqamah, the voice only needs to reach the mosque; therefore, he should say it continuously, not with pauses. (2) From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to Bilal, 'O Bilal, when you give adhan, recite slowly, and when you give iqamah, recite quickly' (b). From this hadith, it is known that adhan should be given with pauses and iqamah quickly. This is mustahabb. Tarassul: speaking with pauses. Hadr: speaking continuously.

Footnote: (a) He commanded Bilal to make the adhan in pairs and the iqamah in odd numbers except 'qad qamat al-salah'.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the manner of reciting adhan and iqamah. The matn states that one should recite slowly (yatarassal) in the adhan and quickly (yahdir) in the iqamah. The commentary explains the reasons: adhan is meant to reach far, so pauses help; iqamah is only for those near the mosque, so it can be said quickly. The Hanafi position is that this is mustahabb (recommended). The text also notes that the majority of imams prefer the iqamah to be in odd numbers (watr), but Hanafis see no karahah if one does it in pairs (shaf'), only a difference in preference. Two hadith proofs are cited: one from Anas about Bilal being commanded to make adhan in pairs and iqamah in odd numbers, and another from Jabir with a direct command from the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Bilal. The Hanafi school follows this ruling as mustahabb, not wajib.

Key Terms
ترسل (tarassul): Speaking with pauses, reciting slowly and deliberately.
حدر (hadr): Speaking quickly and continuously, without pausing.
شفع (shaf'): In pairs; each phrase repeated twice.
وتر (watr): In odd numbers; each phrase repeated once (odd count).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Mustahabb
C) Makruh tahrimi
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Tarassul in adhan and hadr in iqamah are mustahabb (recommended) but not obligatory; the Hanafi school bases this on hadith interpreted with istihsan.

Facing Qibla during Adhan and Iqamah
Ruling on facing qibla while giving adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla during adhan and iqamah, distinguish between sunnah and wajib, and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla during adhan is sunnah, not wajib — the adhan is valid even without it.

Facing the qibla is a recommended practice when calling the adhan and iqamah. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and the difference between the Hanafi position and other schools. Understanding this distinction helps avoid the common misconception that the adhan is invalid if one faces away.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud where the angel faced the qibla when teaching the adhan to Abdullah ibn Zaid.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The angel's action indicates recommendation, not obligation, because it is not accompanied by a command (amr) from the Prophet ﷺ.
Hanafi usul: an action without command indicates istihbab.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider it sunnah mu'akkadah; a minority view holds it wajib. The Hanafi school maintains sunnah.
The practical difference: wajib would require sajdah sahw if omitted; sunnah does not.
5
Evaluate the practical effect
If the mu'adhdhin does not face qibla, the adhan is valid but the sunnah is missed. No repetition or compensation is required.
This ruling prevents unnecessary hardship.

Source Text

(6) And he should face the qibla with both. He should face the qibla when saying adhan and iqamah. Facing the qibla when saying adhan and iqamah is sunnah. But if he does contrary to this, the adhan and iqamah will be valid. However, there will be opposition to the sunnah. (2) There is proof of this in a hadith. Footnote: (c) Abdullah ibn Zaid said: The angel faced the qibla (and gave the adhan).

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah. The matn says 'istayqil bilhi al-qiblah' meaning he should face the qibla while performing both. The commentary clarifies that this is sunnah, not wajib, so if one faces away, the adhan and iqamah are still valid, but the sunnah is missed. The proof is from the hadith about Abdullah ibn Zaid's dream where the angel faced the qibla. This is taken as a basis for the recommendation.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Ka'bah during adhan and iqamah.

Turning Right and Left at Hayya 'ala al-Salah
Ruling on turning the face during adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah action of turning the face during adhan and identify the hadith proof and its legal implication.

Core Idea
Turning the face right at 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and left at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is sunnah, based on the Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah of the adhan: the mu'adhdhin's turning of the face when inviting to prayer and success. The matn prescribes turning the face right and left, and the commentary provides the wisdom and the hadith evidence. Understanding this ruling clarifies a common practice and distinguishes the Hanafi position from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the act being ruled upon: the mu'adhdhin's turning of the face at specific phrases. The matn says 'yuhawwili wajhahu' (he turns his face). The ruling is sunnah (recommended).
Not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud: Bilal turned his neck right and left at the phrases, but did not turn his whole body (lam yastadir).
The hadith is ahad (single narration), thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's approval of Bilal's action indicates recommendation. The phrase 'lawa 'unuqahu' shows only the neck turns, not the entire body.
This is the proof for the Hanafi ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools consider this wajib (obligatory) or even bid'ah. Hanafis hold it as sunnah due to the nature of the proof (zanni).
The practical difference is whether neglecting it is sinful.

(7) Then when he reaches [the words] 'al-salah' and 'al-falah', he turns his face right and left. Adhan for Missed Prayers: Choice and Evidence
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers and apply the choice to a scenario of multiple missed prayers.

Core Idea
For multiple missed prayers, one adhan suffices; iqamah for each is enough.

The matn presents a concise ruling: for a single missed prayer, adhan and iqamah are given. For multiple, there is a choice. This flexibility stems from the Prophetic practice during the Battle of the Trench. We explore the evidence and the reasoning behind the choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving adhan and iqamah for missed prayers (fawa'it). The ruling is mubah (permissible) with a choice between two valid options.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan once and then iqamah for each of four prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha) after the Battle of the Trench.
Reference: Sunan Tirmidhi 79, Sunan Nasa'i 623
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the permissibility? The Prophet's action shows that it is sufficient to give adhan once and then iqamah for each subsequent prayer. This indicates a choice, not an obligation.
The hadith demonstrates the permissibility of the option with one adhan.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that adhan is wajib for each missed prayer. The Hanafi school adopts the choice view, relying on the explicit hadith and the purpose of adhan.
Cross-madhhab difference: wajib vs mubah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is the flexibility (giving adhan once or for each), as it honors the purpose of adhan (calling to prayer) while allowing ease. Both options are valid.
Mufta bihi: permissible to give adhan only for the first.

حاشیہ : (ب) عبد اللہ بن مسعود فرماتے ہیں کہ مشرکین نے حضور کو غزوہ خندق کے دن چار نمازوں سے مشغول کر دیا۔ یہاں تک کہ رات کا کچھ حصہ چلا گیا تو بلال کو حکم دیا تو انہوں نے اذان کہی پھر اقامت کہی اور ظہر کی نماز پڑھی پھر اقامت کہی اور عصر کی نماز پڑھی پھر اقامت کہی اور مغرب کی نماز پڑھی پھر اقامت کہی اور عشا کی نماز پڑھی۔
And he gives adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah. If many prayers are missed, he gives adhan for the first and iqamah, and he has a choice for the second: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah; if he wishes, he suffices with iqamah. If there is one missed prayer, adhan and iqamah will be said. If there are many prayers, he has a choice: whether to give adhan and iqamah for each, or to give adhan only for the first and iqamah for the rest. There is a hadith: Abdullah [ibn Mas'ud] said: The polytheists engaged the Messenger of Allah from four prayers on the day of the Trench until part of the night passed. He commanded Bilal: he gave adhan, then iqamah, and prayed Zuhr; then he gave iqamah and prayed 'Asr; then he gave iqamah and prayed Maghrib; then he gave iqamah and prayed 'Isha' (b). From these hadith, it is known that he gives adhan once and iqamah for the rest, and if he wishes, he may give adhan for each prayer. (2) The purpose of adhan is to call people from outside, and with the first adhan everyone has gathered, so there is little need to give adhan for the remaining prayers. However, since every obligatory prayer begins with adhan, if he gives adhan for each, he may do so.

Footnote: (b) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: ...
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage deals with adhan and iqamah for missed prayers (fawa'it). The matn states that for a single missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah are given. For multiple missed prayers, one has a choice: either give adhan and iqamah for each, or give adhan only for the first and iqamah for the rest. The proof is the hadith of the Battle of the Trench where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan once and then iqamah for each subsequent prayer. The purpose of adhan is to gather people, so once gathered, iqamah suffices. However, because each fard prayer ideally has its own adhan, it is permissible to give adhan for each. The Hanafi position allows flexibility.

Key Terms
فائتة (fa'itah): A missed prayer that is being made up (qada).
مخير (mukhayyar): Having a choice between two permissible options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For multiple missed prayers, a single adhan followed by iqamah for each is sufficient; the Hanafi school permits flexibility based on prophetic practice.

Adhan and Iqamah with Wudu
Ruling with proof on adhan and iqamah and wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing adhan and iqamah with and without wudu, explain the evidence, and identify the difference in ruling between adhan and iqamah.

Core Idea
Adhan without wudu is permissible; iqamah without wudu is makruh but valid. Wudu is sunnah for both.

The performance of adhan and iqamah is closely tied to the prayer they announce. While some schools require wudu for the validity of adhan, the Hanafi school distinguishes between recommendation and permissibility, and further differentiates between adhan and iqamah. This lesson examines the text's ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for adhan with wudu
The matn says 'yanbaghi' (it is appropriate), which indicates a sunnah ruling. The commentary confirms that adhan with wudu is sunnah, and without wudu it is ja'iz (permissible).
The key word 'yanbaghi' signals recommendation, not obligation.
2
Identify the ruling for iqamah with wudu
Similarly, iqamah with wudu is sunnah. However, the commentary explicitly says iqamah without wudu is makruh (disliked), but if done it is valid.
The reason given: iqamah is immediately followed by prayer, so it would be improper for the caller to then go make wudu.
3
Understand the evidence (dalil)
The text cites a hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'None should give adhan except one with wudu.' The Hanafi school interprets this as a recommendation (nadb), not an obligation, because the earlier ruling allows adhan without wudu.
The negation 'la yu'adhdhin' is taken as guidance, not prohibition, due to other evidences.
4
Distinguish between adhan and iqamah
Adhan is dhikr and a call; wudu is recommended. Iqamah is more directly tied to the prayer, so its performance without wudu is considered makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
The practical difference: adhan without wudu is fine; iqamah without wudu is better to avoid, though still valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي ان يؤذن ويقيم على طهر فان اذن غير وضوء جاز. مناسب ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت وضو کے ساتھ کہے۔ پس اگر اذان بغیر وضو کے دیدی تو جائز ہے۔ (1) اذان میں نماز کی طرف بلانا ہے اور ذکر ہے اس لئے وضو کے ساتھ اذان کہے۔ اور اقامت کے بعد تو نماز ہی پڑھنا ہے تو دوسرے لوگ نماز میں مشغول ہوں اور خود نماز کی طرف بلانے والا وضو کرنے جائے تو کتنا بڑا معلوم ہوگا۔ اس لئے اقامت بغیر وضو کے کہنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ اگر کہہ دیا تو اقامت ادا ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله الله قال لا يؤذن الا متوضئ
And it is appropriate that he give adhan and iqamah in a state of purity. If he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible. (1) In adhan, one is calling to prayer and it is dhikr, so adhan should be said with wudu. And after iqamah, prayer is about to begin, so if others are engaged in prayer and the caller himself goes to perform wudu, how bad would that look? Therefore, saying iqamah without wudu is makruh. However, if he says it, the iqamah will be valid. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'None should give adhan except one who has wudu.'
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on being in a state of wudu for adhan and iqamah. The matn says 'yanbaghi an yu'adhdhin wa yuqim 'ala tahr' meaning it is recommended to do so with purity. The commentary clarifies: adhan without wudu is permissible (ja'iz), but iqamah without wudu is makruh (disliked) because it is immediately followed by prayer. If done, both are valid. The proof is a hadith that says 'none should give adhan except one with wudu', which is taken as a recommendation, not obligation.

Key Terms
طهر (tahr): A state of ritual purity (wudu or ghusl). Here, wudu is intended.
ينبغي (yanbaghi): It is appropriate/recommended, indicating a sunnah or mustahabb ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving iqamah without wudu?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is valid but makruh
C) It is highly recommended
D) It is wajib to have wudu

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wudu is sunnah for both adhan and iqamah, but iqamah without wudu is makruh while adhan without wudu is merely permissible.

Adhan for Missed Prayers
Ruling on adhan for multiple missed prayers with option for subsequent prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for multiple missed prayers and apply the evidence from the hadith of the Battle of the Trench.

Core Idea
For multiple missed prayers, one adhan suffices; adhan is for calling, iqamah for beginning.

When a person has missed multiple obligatory prayers, how should they perform the qada? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the Battle of the Trench. This lesson explains the default position and the optional flexibility, supported by a strong hadith proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position for a single missed prayer
For one missed fard prayer, the ruling is to give both adhan and iqamah. This is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Extend to multiple missed prayers: default and option
If multiple prayers are missed, the default is to give adhan only for the first, then iqamah for each subsequent prayer. However, one may choose to give adhan for each if desired.
The option reflects ease and the purpose of adhan.
3
Identify the dalil: hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud
The hadith recounts that during the Battle of the Trench, the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan once, then iqamah for each of the four missed prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha).
The hadith is narrated in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan al-Nasa'i.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of giving adhan once and iqamah for each subsequent prayer directly indicates the permissibility and recommended practice. Since adhan is meant to call people, once they are gathered further adhan is unnecessary.
This reasoning is also supported by the commentary in the source.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some other schools require adhan for each missed prayer. The Hanafi response relies on the explicit practice in the hadith, which is considered a stronger proof.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يؤذن للفائتة ويقيم فان فاتته صلوات اذن للاولى واقام وكان مخيرا في الثانية ان شاء اذن واقم وان شاء اقتصر على الاقامة
بہت کی فائنہ نمازوں کے لئے اذان دی جائے گی اور اقامت کہی جائے گی پس اگر بہت سی نمازیں فوت ہو جائیں تو پہلی نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے۔ اور دوسری نمازوں میں اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو ہر ایک کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے اور اگر چاہے تو صرف اقامت پر اکتفا کرے۔ ا ایک نماز فائتہ ہو اس کے لئے اذان کہی جائے گی اور اقامت کہی جائے گی۔ اور اگر بہت سی نمازیں ہوں تو اختیار ہے چاہے ہر ایک کے لئے اذان دے اور ہر ایک کے لئے اقامت کہے اور چاہے تو صرف پہلی کے لئے اذن دے اور باقی ہر ایک کے لئے اقامت کہے۔ حدیث میں ہے قال عبد الله ان المشرکین شغلوا رسول الله الا الله عن اربع صلوات يوم الخندق حتى ذهب من الليل ماشاء الله فامر بلالا فاذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ثم أقام فصلى المغرب ثم أقام فصلى العشاء (ب) (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل تفوته الصلوات با یتھن یہد اُص ۴۳ نمبر ۷۹ ارنسائی شریف، باب کیف یقضی الفوائت : من الصلوۃ ص ۷۲ نمبر ۶۲۳) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مرتبہ اذان دے اور باقی کے لئے اقامت کہے اور چاہے تو ہر ایک نماز کے لئے اذان بھی کہے ) (۲) اذان کا مقد لوگوں کو باہر سے بلانا ہے اور ہر ایک اذان میں سب جمع ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے باقی نمازوں کے لئے اذان دینے کی چنداں حاجت نہیں ہے۔ البتہ ہر فرض نماز اذان کے ساتھ شروع ہے اس لئے اگر ہر ایک کے لئے اذان دے تو دے سکتا ہے۔
And he gives adhan for the missed (prayer) and says iqamah. If multiple prayers are missed, he gives adhan for the first and says iqamah, and he has a choice for the second: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah, and if he wishes, he restricts to iqamah.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding adhan for missed prayers. The matn states: For a single missed prayer, one gives adhan and iqamah. For multiple missed prayers, the standard practice is to give adhan only for the first, then for each subsequent prayer only iqamah, though one may also give adhan for each if desired. The commentary explains that the purpose of adhan is to call people from outside, and since they are already gathered after the first, further adhan is unnecessary. However, since each fard prayer is initiated with adhan, doing so is permissible. The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about the Battle of the Trench, where the Prophet ordered Bilal to give adhan once and then iqamah for each of the four missed prayers.

Key Terms
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed prayer that is made up after its prescribed time.
اذان (adhān): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, to announce the entry of prayer time.
اقامة (iqāmah): The second call to prayer, recited immediately before the start of the obligatory prayer, similar to adhan but with shorter phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must give adhan and iqamah for each prayer.
B) He gives adhan for the first prayer and iqamah for each, with optional adhan for the rest.
C) He gives iqamah for the first and adhan for the rest.
D) He gives adhan only for the first and no iqamah for the rest.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits one adhan for multiple missed prayers, based on the Prophet's practice, while maintaining flexibility.

Adhan and Wudu: The Recommended State of Purity
Ruling on adhan and iqamah without wudu, and the recommendation to be in a state of purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah without wudu and explain why the hadith is interpreted as a recommendation rather than an obligation.

Core Idea
Adhan without wudu is valid but disliked; wudu is recommended for both adhan and iqamah.

In this lesson, we examine a key hadith that appears to require wudu for adhan. However, the Hanafi school interprets it as a recommendation (tahsini) rather than an obligation. We will explore the reasoning behind this interpretation, the practical implications for the mu'azzin, and the difference between adhan and iqamah. This ruling clarifies the balance between validity and perfection in ritual acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, determine what act is being discussed (adhan and iqamah) and the ruling for each when performed without wudu. The matn states it is permissible but recommends wudu.
Note that the ruling differs slightly between adhan and iqamah in the commentary.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited as proof: 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ' (No one should give adhan except one who is in a state of wudu). This is transmitted by Abu Hurairah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the Hanafi school derives the ruling of recommendation (not obligation) from this hadith. The negation and exception are understood as indicating perfection (tahsini) due to other evidence that adhan without wudu is valid.
The principle is that a command can indicate recommendation when there is evidence against obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other madhhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) interpret this hadith as requiring wudu for validity, making adhan invalid without it.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that adhan and iqamah should be performed with wudu, but if done without, they are valid. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah for adhan with wudu and makruh tanzihi without.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي ان يؤذن ويقيم على طهر فان اذن غير وضوء جاز.
مناسب ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت وضو کے ساتھ کہے۔ پس اگر اذان بغیر وضو کے دیدی تو جائز ہے۔ (1) اذان میں نماز کی طرف بلانا ہے اور ذکر ہے اس لئے وضو کے ساتھ اذان کہے۔ اور اقامت کے بعد تو نماز ہی پڑھنا ہے تو دوسرے لوگ نماز میں مشغول ہوں اور خود نماز کی طرف بلانے والا وضو کرنے جائے تو کتنا بڑا معلوم ہوگا۔ اس لئے اقامت بغیر وضو کے کہنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ اگر کہہ دیا تو اقامت ادا ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله الله قال لا يؤذن الا متوضئ
And it is recommended that he gives adhan and iqamah in a state of purity. If he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the condition of wudu for adhan and iqamah. The matn states: It is recommended to perform adhan and iqamah while in a state of purity (wudu). However, if one gives adhan without wudu, it is still valid. The commentary explains that adhan involves calling people to prayer and is a form of dhikr, so wudu is recommended. For iqamah, performing it without wudu is makruh tanzihi, because the caller, after iqamah, will immediately lead or join the prayer; if he then goes to make wudu, it would appear disrespectful. Nevertheless, if done, the iqamah is valid. The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira in which the Prophet said, 'No one should give adhan except the one who is in a state of wudu.' This shows that wudu is recommended but not obligatory, as the hadith is interpreted as a recommendation.

Key Terms
متوضئ (mutawaddi'): One who has performed wudu (ablution) and is in a state of ritual purity.
مكروه (makrūh): An action that is disliked and discouraged, but not sinful; doing it is valid but leaves one deficient in reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on adhan performed without wudu?
A) It is valid but makruh tanzihi.
B) It is invalid and must be repeated.
C) It is valid and mustahabb.
D) It is invalid unless the mu'azzin is in a state of janabah.

Key Takeaway
Adhan without wudu is valid in the Hanafi school, but it is recommended to be in a state of purity; iqamah without wudu is also valid but more disliked.

Iqamah Without Wudu: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on iqamah without wudu: it is makruh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on iqamah without wudu and identify its classification as makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Iqamah without wudu is valid but disliked — the caller's state matters in adab as-salah.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on performing iqamah (the second call to prayer) without wudu. The Hanafi school considers it valid but disliked, due to the impropriety of calling others to prayer while oneself is in a state of minor impurity. This ruling reflects the school's emphasis on the adab (etiquette) of the mu'azzin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what act is being ruled upon (iqamah without wudu) and what hukm level is assigned (makruh).
The ruling is from a matn stating 'yukrah' (it is disliked).
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The commentary explains that calling others to prayer and then leaving to perform wudu is improper, hence the dislike.
The dislike is due to adab, not invalidity.
3
Distinguish between validity and dislike
Recognize that the iqamah and subsequent prayer are valid; the dislike does not affect validity.
This is a key Hanafi distinction: makruh tanzihi does not render the act invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره ان يقيم على غير وضوء
اور مکروہ ہے کہ اقامت کہے بغیر وضو کے۔ اوپر گزر چکی ہے کہ دوسروں کو نماز کی طرف بلائے اور خود نماز چھوڑ کر وضو کے لئے جائے تو کتنی بری بات ہے؟
And it is disliked that he says iqamah without wudu.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that iqamah without wudu is makruh. The commentary explains the reason: the caller is inviting others to prayer, and if he then leaves to perform wudu while others proceed with the prayer, that would be highly improper. Hence, it is disliked to perform iqamah without wudu. This is based on the earlier discussion.

Key Terms
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing iqamah without wudu?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but makruh (disliked).
C) It is valid and there is no dislike.
D) It is invalid only if the person is in Janabah.

Key Takeaway
Iqamah without wudu is valid but makruh tanzihi; the adab of the call requires the caller to be in a state of purity.

Adhan Before Time and the Fajr Exception
Ruling on adhan before time with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling for adhan before time and explain the Fajr exception according to Abu Yusuf, citing the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
Adhan before time is haram, but a pre-dawn call for Fajr is allowed to wake worshippers.

This lesson examines a key ruling in the Hanafi school: adhan is meant to announce the prayer time, so giving it early misleads people and is prohibited. However, an exception is made for Fajr based on practice from the Prophet's era. We will explore the evidence and the differing views within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? What is the basic hukm (prohibition or permissibility)?
The act is giving adhan before the prescribed time for prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the commentary cite? Identify the hadith and its source.
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from Bukhari and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith support the Fajr exception? What specific wording or context is used?
The hadith describes Bilal's adhan as being at night to wake people, not for the actual prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Who within the Hanafi school disagrees, and what is their argument?
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani oppose any adhan before time, including Fajr.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) and why?
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf, allowing a pre-dawn adhan when needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يؤذن لصلوة قبل وقتها الا فى الفجر عند ابي يوسف.
نہیں الآن دی جائے نماز کے لئے اس کے وقت سے پہلے مگر فجر میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک (۱) اذان دینے کا مقصد وقت بتانا ہے۔ لیکن وقت سے پہلے اذان دینے سے وقت کی تجہیل ہوگی ۔ اس لئے وقت سے پہلے اذان نہ دی جائے (۲) مدینہ طیبہ میں فجر کی اذان وقت سے پہلے دی جاتی تھی وہ تہجد والوں کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے اور جو تہجد پڑھ چکے ہیں ان کو آرام کرنے کی اطلاع دینے کے لئے تھی۔ چنانچہ مدینہ طیبہ اور مکہ مکرمہ کی طرح تہجد پڑھنے والے کثرت سے ہوں تو ان کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے اذان دی جاسکتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ فجر کی نماز کے لئے عبداللہ بن مکتوب دوسری اذان دیا کرتے تھے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود عن النبي الله قال لا يمنعن احدكم او احدا منكم اذان بلال من سحوره فانه يؤذن او ينادى بليل ليرجع قائمكم ولينبه ناتمکم (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاذان قبل الفجر ص ۷ ۸ نمبر ۶۲ رنسائی شریف، باب الاذان فی غیر وقت الصلو وص ۷۵ نمبر ۶۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رات میں حضرت بلال کی اذان فجر کی نماز کے لئے نہیں تھی، تہجد والوں کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے تھی۔ اسی لئے نماز کے وقت حضرت عبداللہ ابن مکتوب دوبارہ اذان دیا کرتے تھے۔ حدیث میں ہے (۳) عن عائشة عن النبي صلى الله انه قال ان بلالا يؤذن بليل فكلوا واشربوا حتى يؤذن ابن ام مکتوم (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاذان قبل الفجر ص ۷ ۸ نمبر ۶۲۲ متر ندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الاذان باللیل ص۵۰ نمبر ۲۰۳) (۴) وقت سے پہلے اذن دینے سے اذان لوٹانی پڑے گی حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر ان بلالا اذن بليل فامره النبي الله ان ينادى ان العبد قد نام ( و ) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الاذان باللیل
And adhan should not be given for a prayer before its time, except for Fajr according to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding adhan before the prescribed time. The matn states: Adhan should not be given before the time of prayer, except for Fajr, according to Imam Abu Yusuf. The commentary explains that the purpose of adhan is to announce the time, so giving it early defeats that purpose. However, in Madinah, an early adhan for Fajr was given by Bilal to wake those performing tahajjud and to indicate that it is time to rest for those who have finished. This practice is permitted when there are many people engaged in night worship, as in Makkah and Madinah. Therefore, the second adhan by Ibn Umm Maktum at the correct time was the actual call for Fajr. Hadiths are cited to support this distinction: Bilal's adhan was before dawn to wake people, and the proper adhan for Fajr is after dawn. If adhan is given before time, it must be repeated. The hadith of Ibn Umar shows that when Bilal gave adhan early, the Prophet ordered him to call out that he had mistaken.

Key Terms
وقت (waqt): The prescribed time for a specific prayer as determined by the Shari'ah.
فجر (fajr): The dawn prayer; its time begins at true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid and no further adhan is needed.
B) It is permissible only if it is followed by a second adhan at the correct time.
C) It is invalid and must be repeated immediately.
D) It is recommended but requires repetition.

Key Takeaway
Adhan before time is generally prohibited, but a pre-dawn call for Fajr is allowed as a distinct sunna to wake worshippers, provided the actual adhan is given at its time.

Adhan Before Fajr: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Ruling that adhan before the time is not allowed, except for Fajr according to Imam Abu Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions regarding adhan before Fajr, explain the proofs cited by each side, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Adhan before Fajr is valid according to Imam Abu Yusuf due to Madinan practice, but invalid per Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the adhan may be given before the prescribed time for Fajr prayer. While the general rule prohibits adhan before the time, Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for Fajr based on the practice of the Prophet's ﷺ time in Madinah. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you appreciate how differences in evidence (hadith vs. qiyas) can produce divergent rulings within the same madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and the exception for Fajr
Identify the overarching ruling: adhan should not be given before the time for any prayer. Then note the exception: 'except in Fajr, according to Abu Yusuf.'
The exception is only for Fajr and only according to Abu Yusuf; Abu Hanifa holds no exception.
2
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Recognize that the intā-Hanafi dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa (general prohibition for all prayers) and Imam Abu Yusuf (exception for Fajr).
Abu Yusuf's position is supported by Imam Shafi'i as well.
3
Examine the evidence for Abu Yusuf's position
Analyze the hadiths about Bilal's nighttime call and the practice of two adhans in Madinah. Understand that the early call was a wake-up for tahajjud, and the actual Fajr adhan by Ibn Umm Maktum came later.
The hadith 'Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan' (Bukhari) supports the distinction.
4
Examine the counter-evidence and Abu Hanifa's response
Consider the hadith where the Prophet told Bilal not to give adhan until dawn is clearly visible. Understand that Abu Hanifa views this as a general prohibition, while Abu Yusuf sees it as a correction of a specific mistake.
The Prophet's order to apologize ('Indeed the servant has slept') indicates that Bilal's early call was not proper adhan for Fajr.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a mu'azzin gives adhan before Fajr time, according to Abu Yusuf the adhan is valid and does not need to be repeated. According to Abu Hanifa, it is invalid and must be repeated later.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of Abu Yusuf, making early Fajr adhan valid in practice.

Source Text

[۱۵۸] (۱۲) ولا يؤذن لصلوة قبل وقتها الا فى الفجر عند ابي يوسف. (۱) اذان دینے کا مقصد وقت بتانا ہے۔ لیکن وقت سے پہلے اذان دینے سے وقت کی تجہیل ہوگی ۔ اس لئے وقت سے پہلے اذان نہ دی جائے (۲) مدینہ طیبہ میں فجر کی اذان وقت سے پہلے دی جاتی تھی وہ تہجد والوں کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے اور جو تہجد پڑھ چکے ہیں ان کو آرام کرنے کی اطلاع دینے کے لئے تھی۔ چنانچہ مدینہ طیبہ اور مکہ مکرمہ کی طرح تہجد پڑھنے والے کثرت سے ہوں تو ان کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے اذان دی جاسکتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ فجر کی نماز کے لئے عبداللہ بن مکتوب دوسری اذان دیا کرتے تھے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود عن النبي الله قال لا يمنعن احدكم او احدا منكم اذان بلال من سحوره فانه يؤذن او ينادى بليل ليرجع قائمكم ولينبه ناتمکم (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاذان قبل الفجر ص ۷ ۸ نمبر ۶۲ رنسائی شریف، باب الاذان فی غیر وقت الصلو وص ۷۵ نمبر ۶۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رات میں حضرت بلال کی اذان فجر کی نماز کے لئے نہیں تھی، تہجد والوں کو بیدار کرنے کے لئے تھی۔ اسی لئے نماز کے وقت حضرت عبداللہ ابن مکتوب دوبارہ اذان دیا کرتے تھے۔ حدیث میں ہے (۳) عن عائشة عن النبي صلى الله عليه انه قال ان بلالا يؤذن بليل فكلوا واشربوا حتى يؤذن ابن ام مکتوم (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاذان قبل الفجر ص ۷ ۸ نمبر ۶۲۲ متر ندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الاذان باللیل ص۵۰ نمبر ۲۰۳) (۴) وقت سے پہلے اذن دینے سے اذان لوٹانی پڑے گی حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر ان بلالا اذن بليل فامره النبي الله ان ينادى ان العبد قد نام ( و ) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الاذان باللیل حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کہ اذان نہ دے مگر وضو کی حالت میں (ب) آپ نے فرمایا تم میں سے کسی ایک کو بلال کی اذان سحری سے نہ رو کے اس لئے کہ وہ اذان دیتے ہیں رات میں تا کہ تم میں سے تہجد میں کھڑے ہونے والے لوگ واپس ہو جائیں اور تم میں سے سونے والے بیدار ہو جائیں (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کہ بلال رات میں اذان دیتے ہیں اس لئے سحری کھاتے پیتے رہو یہاں تک کہ عبد اللہ بن مکتوم اذان دے (د) حضرت عبداللہ ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت بلال نے رات میں اذان دے دی تو حضور نے ان کو حکم دیا کہ پکار کر کہو کہ میں نیند میں تھا۔

ص ۵۰ نمبر ۲۰۳ را ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الاذان قبل دخول الوقت ص ۸۶ نمبر ۵۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے پہلے حضرت بلال نے اذان دی تو حضور نے ان کو لوگوں کے سامنے معذرت کرنے کے لئے کہا کہ ان العبد قد نام کہو (۵) ان رسول الله الله قال له لا تؤذن حتى ليتبين لك الفجر هكذا ومد يديه عرضا (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الاذان قبل دخول الوقت ص ۸۶ نمبر ۵۳۴) فائدہ تاہم اوپر کی احادیث کی وجہ سے امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ فجر سے پہلے اذان دیدی تو اذان ادا ہو جائے گی۔ دوسری نمازوں میں اذان ادا نہیں ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے حضرت بلال سے فرمایا کہ اذان نہ دو جب تک کہ فجر تمہارے لئے واضح نہ ہو جائے اس طرح ۔
[158] (12) And adhan should not be given for prayer before its time except in Fajr, according to Abu Yusuf. (1) The purpose of adhan is to indicate the time. But giving adhan before the time causes confusion about the time. Therefore adhan should not be given before the time. (2) In Madinah Tayyibah, the adhan for Fajr used to be given before the time; it was to wake up those praying tahajjud and to inform those who had finished tahajjud to take rest. Thus, if there are many tahajjud pray-ers like in Madinah and Makkah, adhan may be given to wake them. That is why Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum used to give a second adhan for Fajr prayer. A hadith: from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud from the Prophet ﷺ, he said: 'Do not let any of you be prevented by Bilal's adhan from your suhur, for he gives adhan or calls out at night so that those of you who are standing (in prayer) may return, and to wake those of you who are sleeping.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter on adhan before Fajr, p. 78, no. 62; Nasa'i, chapter on adhan at other than prayer time, p. 75, no. 642) From this hadith it is understood that Bilal's adhan at night was not for Fajr prayer, but to wake the tahajjud pray-ers. For that reason, at the time of prayer, Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum used to give adhan again. A hadith: (3) from A'isha from the Prophet ﷺ, he said: 'Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan.' (c) (Bukhari, chapter on adhan before Fajr, p. 78, no. 622; Tirmidhi, chapter on adhan at night, p. 50, no. 203) (4) If adhan is given before the time, the adhan must be repeated. A hadith: from Ibn Umar that Bilal gave adhan at night, so the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to call out: 'Indeed the servant has slept.' (w) (Tirmidhi, chapter on adhan at night, p. 50, no. 203; Abu Dawud, chapter on adhan before entry of time, p. 86, no. 532) Footnote: (a) He said: 'Do not give adhan except with wudu.' (b) He said: 'Do not let any of you be prevented by Bilal's adhan from your suhur, because he gives adhan at night so that those of you standing (in prayer) may return and those of you sleeping may be woken.' (c) He said: 'Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan.' (d) Abdullah ibn Umar says: Bilal gave adhan at night, so the Prophet ordered him to call out: 'I was asleep.' 
[PAGE_126] page 50, no. 203; Abu Dawud, chapter on adhan before entry of time, p. 86, no. 532) From this hadith it is learned that when Bilal gave adhan before the time, the Prophet ordered him to make an excuse to the people, saying 'Indeed the servant has slept.' (5) The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to him: 'Do not give adhan until it becomes clear to you that the dawn is like this,' and he extended his hands sideways. (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on adhan before entry of time, p. 86, no. 534) Benefit: Nevertheless, because of the above hadiths, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i say that if adhan is given before Fajr, the adhan is valid. For other prayers, it is not valid. Footnote: (a) He said to Bilal: 'Do not give adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this.'
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of giving adhan before the prescribed time. The general rule is that adhan should only be given after the time begins, because its purpose is to indicate the time. Giving it early causes confusion. However, Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for Fajr prayer, based on the practice in Madinah where an early adhan was given to wake people for tahajjud and suhur. The evidence includes hadiths about Bilal’s nighttime call, which was not a Fajr adhan but a wake-up call, and the second adhan by Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum at the actual time. Other hadiths show that when Bilal gave adhan too early, the Prophet ordered him to apologize and not to give adhan until dawn was clearly visible. Despite these apparent counterexamples, the commentary concludes that Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i hold that an early Fajr adhan is valid (the call counts as adhan), while for other prayers it is not valid. This is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa (implied) and the general rule restrict adhan to after time entry, whereas Abu Yusuf allows the early Fajr adhan due to the established practice.

Key Terms
تجهيل (tajhil): Causing confusion about the time; giving adhan before the proper time misleads people.
تہجد (tahajjud): The night vigil prayer performed after sleeping, usually before Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, for which prayer is adhan permissible before its time?
A) All prayers
B) Fajr only
C) None
D) Maghrib and Fajr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal difference on early Fajr adhan; the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is valid, based on the established practice of Madinah.

Adhan Before Fajr Time: Hanafi and Shafi'i Views
Inter-madhhab dispute on adhan before Fajr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i on adhan before Fajr time and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
For Fajr, adhan before time is valid per Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i; for other prayers it is not.

This lesson examines a specific dispute regarding the validity of the call to prayer (adhan) when given before the prescribed time. While general Islamic legal principles require adhan to be announced at the onset of prayer time, a notable exception is made for the Fajr prayer by some scholars. We will analyze the hadith evidence and the different interpretations that lead to this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The disputed issue is whether an adhan given before the entry of prayer time is valid. The focus is on Fajr prayer.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i
According to the passage, both Imam Abu Yusuf (Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the Fajr adhan, when given before true dawn, is still considered a valid adhan. However, this ruling is specific to Fajr and does not apply to other prayers.
The position of Imam Abu Hanifa himself is not mentioned here; it may differ.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage cites two hadiths from Abu Dawud. The first hadith shows that when Bilal gave the adhan early, the Prophet instructed him to tell people he had slept, implying the adhan was not on time. The second hadith contains a direct command to wait until dawn is clearly visible. These hadiths are used by both sides but interpreted differently.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of this dispute: if the Fajr adhan is given early, according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, it is valid and does not need repetition. According to a stricter view (possibly Abu Hanifa), it may be invalid and require repetition.
The passage does not provide a tarjih (preference) between the views.
5
Apply the ruling to other prayers
Both scholars agree that for prayers other than Fajr, an adhan given before time is not valid. This distinction is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول ۱۲۱ كتاب الصلوة ص ۵۰ نمبر ۲۰۳ را ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الاذان قبل دخول الوقت ص ۸۶ نمبر ۵۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے پہلے حضرت بلال نے اذان دی تو حضور نے ان کو لوگوں کے سامنے معذرت کرنے کے لئے کہا کہ ان العبد قد نام کہو (۵) ان رسول الله الله قال له لا تؤذن حتى ليتبين لك الفجر هكذا ومد يديه عرضا (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الاذان قبل دخول الوقت ص ۸۶ نمبر ۵۳۴) فائدہ تاہم اوپر کی احادیث کی وجہ سے امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ فجر سے پہلے اذان دیدی تو اذان ادا ہو جائے گی۔ دوسری نمازوں میں اذان ادا نہیں ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے حضرت بلال سے فرمایا کہ اذان نہ دو جب تک کہ فجر تمہارے لئے واضح نہ ہو جائے اس طرح ۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 1, page 121. Book of Prayer. (Reference: Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Adhan qabla dukhul al-waqt, p. 86 no. 532) From this hadith it is known that before the time, Hadrat Bilal gave the adhan, so the Prophet told him to excuse himself before the people by saying 'Indeed the servant slept.' (5) The Messenger of Allah said to him: 'Do not give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this' and he spread his hands wide (a) (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Adhan qabla dukhul al-waqt, p. 86 no. 534). Benefit: Nevertheless, due to the above hadiths, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i say that if the adhan for Fajr is given before its time, the adhan is fulfilled. For other prayers, the adhan is not fulfilled. Footnote: (a) He said to Hadrat Bilal: 'Do not give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you, like this.'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of adhan given before the prescribed time. It begins by citing a hadith from Abu Dawud in which Bilal gave the adhan before Fajr time, and the Prophet instructed him to inform the people that he had slept, implying that the adhan was not valid. Another hadith shows the Prophet explicitly telling Bilal to wait until dawn is clearly visible. The author then presents a 'fa'idah' (benefit): despite these hadiths, Imam Abu Yusuf (a leading Hanafi jurist) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that if the adhan for Fajr is given before time, it is still considered valid adhan, but this is not the case for other prayers. The Hanafi position is not fully stated here, but the passage implies a difference of opinion. The footnote clarifies the Prophet's instruction to Bilal.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, announced to signal the entry of prayer time.
فجر (fajr): The dawn prayer; its time begins at true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq).
فائدة (fa'idah): A beneficial note or additional ruling derived from the discussion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The adhan is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The adhan is valid for Fajr but not for other prayers.
C) The adhan is valid for all prayers.
D) The adhan is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The adhan for Fajr prayer, if given before its time, is considered valid by Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, but this does not apply to other prayers.
